Current Commentary

Compatriots, Quickly Awaken and Rise Up

Today, the Central Government issued a nationwide order to mourn for the compatriots in our Northeast who were brutally killed by the Japanese military and to commemorate the national humiliation. I

Our country's people today stand under the half-lowered flag fluttering in the crisp autumn wind. Silently ponder the destruction of our great rivers and mountains, and silently ponder the current crisis of our nation. As warm-blooded men, you should be heartbroken and weep, and as warm-blooded men, you should bravely rise up.

Today's affairs: Crying is not enough to save the country, rash actions are not enough to save the country, and waiting for help is even less enough to save the country. Saving the country lies in active and effective actions, and in the unity of all people.

The race is declining and the mountains and rivers are broken. All our compatriots in the country should cry out in unison. If you don't cry now, what else is there to cry about? However, shedding all the blood and tears will not wash away the shame of our country and our nation today, and will not make up for the current great disaster. If reason has not been obliterated, if mankind has not died out, we hope that the world will effectively restrain this act of taking advantage of people's difficulties. However, waiting for someone to save you is ultimately a possibility that is difficult to realize. Justice is often in the hands of the strong. Who is willing to come forward and speak out for justice? Therefore, today's affairs can be decided with one sentence: only self-help can save oneself, and only struggle can lead to survival. Retreating is suicide, that is, waiting for destruction. The ambitions of the Japanese will not stop until they include our country and destroy our nation. The atrocities in Shenyang, the attacks in Jilin, killing our soldiers and civilians, occupying our land. We have already resisted and retreated. However, the Japanese atrocities have not diminished slightly, but have intensified. If we retreat to Shanhaiguan, the Japanese will also press to Shanhaiguan. Suppose we retreat to Beijing, retreat to Shanghai, retreat to Nanjing, and the Japanese still advance step by step. Will we continue to retreat without resisting? Yesterday, the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters sent a telegram to the Central Government, saying, "Even if we try our best to retreat, there must be a limit to the retreat. Even if we are willing to be slaughtered, we should choose the method of slaughter." The words are extremely painful. Fighting to death is death, and waiting to die is also death. Which one is better? We should choose for ourselves. The alliance under the city can be done once, but not again. If we follow the old ways and sit idly by without taking the initiative, will we allow the civilized ancient country and the great mountains and rivers to be destroyed by our hands today? We have already complied with the spirit and creed of the Pact of Paris first. Only self-defense can save oneself, and only warm blood can wash away shame. Our country is at a time when it can no longer tolerate or allow any concession, and should strive to resist violence and seek self-defense. In other words, it should make a back-to-the-wall battle for self-defense for the sake of defending the country and defending the nation.

The people of the whole country should, in the face of this great disaster, follow Mr. Sun Yat-sen's principle of "peaceful struggle", adopt a calm attitude, have the determination to die, eliminate internal disputes and resist foreign aggression, and avoid rash actions and useless sacrifices. But if everyone has this awareness and determination, when the bugle sounds, they can rise up at any time to serve the country. At this time, all sectors of agriculture, industry, and commerce should intensify their work to prepare for contingencies. As for the youth, the lifeline of the country is at stake, and the responsibility on their shoulders is even more arduous. At this time, they should thoroughly awaken, rise up and struggle, actively temper their body and mind, strengthen their will, read without forgetting to save the country, and save the country without forgetting to read. They should learn from the spirit of the emerging nations of Germany, Turkey, and the Soviet Union, endure hardships and hone themselves, make effective struggles, make proper sacrifices, and make permanent persistence.

The situation is critical and disaster is imminent. Fortune and misfortune, survival and death, are determined today. Natural disasters and foreign enemies can all destroy us. If we want to not be destroyed, we can only save ourselves. Napoleon once said, "There is a giant in the East who is fast asleep. Let him sleep, because when he wakes up, he can immediately shake the whole world." Today's severe natural disasters and foreign troubles are the alarm bells to wake up our nation's dream. With our country's vast land and abundant resources and people, if we resolutely rise up, what shame cannot be washed away, and what disaster cannot be eliminated? The current situation is not to be feared or lamented. But it is necessary to awaken, unite, and fight together.

Domestic Important Telegrams Two

Central Announcement

A Message to Our Compatriots Throughout the Nation

Achieve True Unity

Remain Steadfast and Calm

Work with Redoubled Effort

(Nanjing) In light of Japan's sudden violent occupation of our Northeastern territories, the Central Government, recognizing the shared national crisis facing all compatriots, issues the following message to the nation: Japan, taking advantage of our internal strife, compounded by sudden natural disasters causing death, displacement, and overwhelming relief efforts, has launched a violent invasion. On the 19th, they forcibly seized Shenyang, and since then, crucial areas of Liaoning and Jilin have been ravaged. Their acts of aggression continue unabated. Such barbaric conduct is not only prohibited by international laws and treaties, but also constitutes an unprecedented occurrence in world history. Our nation suffers unparalleled humiliation, and our people endure immense aggression. All those with a sense of honor are filled with outrage. Our Party, adhering to the teachings of the late Premier, revolted to save the nation. The Central Government, in fulfilling its duty, will make its utmost effort to avert this unprecedented crisis. We firmly believe that justice has not been extinguished and that aggression will be restrained. We are also confident that our compatriots, fueled by righteous indignation, are prepared to perish rather than surrender. When the final, necessary moment arrives, they will shed their last drop of blood to defend our national integrity and the survival of our people. We wish to convey to all our compatriots throughout the nation that, facing this extraordinary event, the nation must rely on the united strength of all its people. It is especially crucial to identify a common path forward. Saving the nation and resisting foreign aggression is the most arduous and critical task in the world. Precisely because it is critical, we must not treat it lightly. Precisely because it is arduous, we must execute it with a highly robust organization. Our nation has suffered years of hardship, and its strength is insufficient, leading to danger and humiliation. This situation does not arise from a single cause. The most prominent factor is the lack of discipline in collective action. This current foreign invasion is unprecedented in its severity. To ensure that justice prevails and aggression is curbed, we must act in unison, proceed in step, heed unified command, and maintain strict discipline. Only then can we generate comprehensive strength to achieve concrete results. Under these principles, we wish to point out the following matters to our compatriots: (1) We must achieve true unity. We must recognize that the paramount task at hand is to save the nation, and completing this task is of utmost importance. Under the grand principle of safeguarding national interests, we must strictly avoid antagonism based on class, region, or even differing views and emotions. All actions in the world are based on unity. Those who fight individually against a formidable enemy will surely fail. Those who engage in mutual recrimination during a major crisis will surely perish. Therefore, all words and actions must genuinely maintain national unity. (2) We must remain steadfast and calm. We must recognize that the responsibility upon our shoulders is extremely grave. A precarious situation cannot be reversed by empty slogans or by impulsive emotional outbursts. Therefore, we must refine our fervent emotions into unwavering strength. We must be prepared to make sacrifices at all times. All matters must be executed with established order, and we must strictly avoid boastfulness. We must be aware that others despise us for our weakness and timidity; therefore, we must strive for resoluteness. Aware that others hope for internal strife, we must be cautious of treacherous schemes. (3) We must work with redoubled effort. Whether it is the nation or the individual, we must dedicate ourselves to hard work and intensify our efforts. Amidst coping with the crisis, we must cultivate the foundations of the nation. We must recognize that the effort to ensure national survival cannot cease for a moment. At this moment, we must deeply reflect on the reasons for our nation's weakness. Therefore, on one hand, the government must continue to exert effort in suppressing bandits and providing disaster relief. On the other hand, our people, whether farmers, workers, merchants, or students, must not neglect their respective duties for even a moment. Only when the entire nation profoundly understands and genuinely prepares to make sacrifices at any time can the national crisis be resolved. Otherwise, disarray will not contribute to saving the nation, and losses will only benefit the enemy. The above three points are guiding principles for our entire nation to abide by. With the crisis at hand, we can no longer afford to hesitate or slacken. We earnestly hope that we will maintain unwavering resolve, uphold firm discipline, and be prepared to die. We must engage in sustained struggle, saving the nation is saving ourselves, defending against aggression is defending our homeland. Turning misfortune into fortune depends on the efforts of our entire nation. Let us strive together. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

Beijing City Convenes

City-Wide Party Member Congress

Chairman Chiang Delivers a Solemn Speech

Do Not Allow Spirits to Wane; Avoid Frivolous Actions

Temporarily Endure with Patience; Prepare for Final Resolve

(Nanjing) The Japanese military's occupation of our Eastern Provinces has ignited nationwide outrage. The entire body of Party members in Beijing held a city-wide Party member congress at the Central Auditorium at 9:00 AM on the 22nd, with over six thousand attendees. All were filled with indignation and vowed to avenge this humiliation. Members of the Central Committee present included Chiang Kai-shek, Dai Chuanxian, Zhu Jiahua, Chen Bulei, Zhang Daofan, Yu Jingtang, Fang Juehui, and others. The atmosphere throughout was unusually tense, and order was maintained. After Chairman Chen Haicheng reported the purpose of the meeting, it was followed by a report from Chairman Chiang as follows:

Meeting Circumstances of the Nanjing City-Wide Party Member Congress

The abrupt military action taken by Japan in our three Northeastern provinces, forcibly occupying our Shenyang, Changchun, Andong, Yingkou, and other crucial areas of Liaoning Province, is unprecedented in the international arena. Our nation has suffered a humiliating and grievous insult. All comrades and compatriots must deeply recognize this, rise up in unity, and save our nation from peril. Moreover, it is especially important to study the context of this issue from a broad perspective to grasp the true situation and devise a response. This Japanese act of aggression not only undermines peace in the Far East but also threatens world peace, and the situation is extremely grave. Therefore, we must firmly resolve to respond with steadfastness. In my opinion, this Japanese act of aggression can be seen as a test of the following two points:

(1) A test of whether there is justice or fairness in the international community and whether the nations of the world are determined to curb tyranny and ensure world peace. This Japanese action not only exploits our vulnerability and violates international morality but also gravely undermines the spirit of the Covenant of the League of Nations and the Kellogg-Briand Pact. Both of these treaties were established by various nations to ensure world peace, and I firmly believe that all members of the League of Nations and signatories of the Kellogg-Briand Pact will appropriately judge Japan's act of aggression in violation of these treaties.

(2) This incident can test whether our nation can unite and unleash a spirit of patriotism to resist foreign aggression. I recall that the Japanese have a book titled "The Escalation of the Manchurian Problem," which roughly describes the Chinese people as being disunited and indifferent to national affairs. It suggests that the Chinese people outside the war zone during the Sino-Japanese War and the Boxer Rebellion seemed unconcerned. The people of the South were bystanders to events in the North, and the people of the North were also unconcerned about events in the South. This is the general idea of the book. Therefore, Japan dares to openly invade because it truly regards our people as insignificant. This is deeply regrettable. Whether our nation can unite as a whole, with the entire country of one mind, and unleash a genuine spirit of patriotism to save the nation from this grave national crisis is also a significant test. I firmly believe that all our people, recognizing the fundamental importance of this day for the survival of our nation, will rise up in unison and save our nation from peril, thereby thwarting Japan's ambitions and proving its observation wrong. However, when a major event occurs in the nation, the spirit of the people must not be allowed to wane or become disorganized. In particular, actions must avoid frivolity. Strength is born from organization. We must act in unison, proceed in step, maintain strict discipline, obey unified command, and be of one mind and one heart in engaging in a fight to the death. Only then can we generate effectiveness. We must never act alone and fall into disunity. Now that Japanese aggression has occurred, it has been five days. The Central Government has conducted careful study and decided on the steps to be taken. At this time, world opinion has generally recognized that Japan is being unreasonable. Our people must, at this moment, be united, place justice against power, and use peace to counter barbarism. We must endure the pain, suppress our anger, and temporarily adopt an attitude of enduring with patience while awaiting the judgment of international justice. All our comrades, adhering to the Three Principles of the People, should revolutionize and save the nation and should have the resolve to disregard life and death to preserve the survival of our people. However, the survival of the nation is of paramount importance. At this time, we must urge the people to strictly abide by order, obey the government, respect discipline, and avoid reckless actions outside the bounds, instead engaging in a well-ordered and methodical struggle. To endure with patience for the moment is by no means to surrender. If international treaties and trust are rendered ineffective, and peace becomes hopeless, reaching the point where endurance is unbearable and should not be endured, then the Central Government has made its final determination and final preparations. At that time, it will surely lead the entire nation, preferring to be shattered like jade, and use the strength of four hundred million people to defend the survival of our nation and the integrity of our country. I have dedicated myself to the revolution, placing life and death aside long ago. At this moment of crisis and survival, I will surely exist with the nation and perish with the nation. I will stand at the forefront of the people as their vanguard, sharing the national crisis and fulfilling my duty. I hope that all comrades will understand this intention and widely convey it to our people. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

(Nanjing) The city-wide Party member congress held in Beijing on the 22nd has passed resolutions, including: (1) A telegram to military and political leaders across the nation to cease internal strife and jointly resist foreign aggression; (2) A request to the Central Government to immediately declare a break in relations with Japan and prepare for war; (3) A telegram to Party branches at all levels and all Party members across the nation to immediately organize Party member volunteer armies to save the nation; (4) A telegram to the people across the nation to be the government's support in a unified general mobilization for war against Japan; (5) An urgent telegram to the Central Government and Comrade Zhang Xueliang to relay to all officers and soldiers in the Northeast a pledge to resist Japanese aggression and not yield ground to preserve our territory and protect national sovereignty; (6) A telegram to the people across the nation for a permanent economic break with Japan; (7) A telegram to the people across the nation and Party branches at all levels at home and abroad to unite the entire Party and the nation to jointly save the nation from foreign crisis. After the meeting adjourned, the entire presidium of the congress went to Hu Hanmin's residence to urge him to assume his duties immediately and jointly plan for the nation's survival. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

(Nanjing) News from the Beining Railway on the 21st: (1) Trains on this railway still run to Huanggu Village Station, but the military police at that station have been forced to withdraw. People are panicking and food is scarce. (2) Three Japanese aircraft flew over Xinmin County this afternoon. The Japanese consul informed the county magistrate, ordering our garrison to withdraw from the county. (3) The Datong Line is still open to traffic. Multiple Japanese aircraft have been bombing or strafing with machine guns at Dahushan, destroying barracks and killing dozens. (4) The situation in Yingkou is still unclear. According to reports, one Japanese warship is present, and the tracks at Tianzhuangtai and the Dawazhan station in Huwo Village have been destroyed. (5) Huludao is peaceful. (6) The Shenyang office is still under Japanese military surveillance. (7) Only twenty foreign members of the Sino-foreign press corps have arrived in Shenyang, and they are being questioned very strictly. They have not been granted permission by the Japanese military commander to investigate in various places, nor are they being received. The dry plates in their cameras have been confiscated, and photography is prohibited. There have been many casualties among military police and civilians. Part of Northeastern University has been destroyed, and students have been expelled. There have been reports of deaths and injuries. Most of the munitions and machinery stored in the arsenal have been transported away by the Japanese military, and many factory workers have been killed or injured. The official silver house and the Bank of Communications have been sealed, and the cash has been transported away. Major residences have been ransacked, and the documents of various institutions have been burned. Prisoners have all been released. The Japanese military has issued a notice in the city prohibiting Chinese from hindering their actions, under penalty of death. (8) It was recently reported that the city of Jilin was occupied by the Japanese military at 3:00 PM today, with a considerable number of deaths and injuries. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

Military and Civilian Casualties in Shenyang

Bodies Entirely Cremated by the Japanese

(Tianjin) According to a telegram from Huanggu Village, no one dares to claim the bodies of the military and civilians killed in Shenyang. They have now been transported to the suburbs and cremated by Japanese soldiers. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

Telegram from the Longkou Chamber of Commerce Reports

Japanese Plainclothes Troops Landing

(Nanjing) A certain agency received a telegram from the Longkou Chamber of Commerce stating that over a hundred Japanese plainclothes troops have landed in Longkou and are requesting our troops to move away. In addition, the Japanese ship "Ryūhei Maru" is carrying over a hundred Japanese army troops and appears to be entering the port. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

Devastation in Shenyang City

(Beiping) According to a certain dignitary who arrived in Beiping from Shenyang today, all institutions in Shenyang City are closed, and the documents have been burned. Interiors of the institutions were destroyed, and Japanese notices were posted at the entrances stating that the Japanese military has occupied the area and violators will be sentenced to death. Chinese who resist or even look at the entrances will be stabbed to death. The Bank of Communications, Frontier Development Bank, and official silver house were all opened and looted. Residences of dignitaries in the commercial area were ransacked and emptied. Citizens have nowhere to buy rice, and many have starved to death in recent days. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

British and French Ministers

Visit Zhang Xueliang Separately

British and French Military Attaches to Visit Shenyang for Investigation

(Beiping) The British Minister, Lampson, and the French Minister, Wilden, visited Zhang Xueliang separately this afternoon for lengthy talks, expressing great concern. The naval attache of the British embassy, Brown, and the army attache of the French embassy, Joutard, and the air force attache, Fitte, left for Tianjin by car this afternoon and will proceed to Shenyang to conduct a detailed investigation. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

(Beiping) The British attache, D'Arcy, is going to Shenyang tonight to investigate the truth of the Shenyang incident and will report truthfully to his government. The British naval officer, Titcoat, is going to Tianjin today. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

Japan to Send Aircraft

To Bomb Our Garrison Areas

(Tianjin) According to a telegram from Harbin, it is rumored that the Japanese military will dispatch a large number of aircraft to bomb our garrison areas, dropping bombs. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

Pingjin Press Corps to Shenyang

Part of the Group Turns Back Midway

(Tianjin) Of the seventeen members of the Tianjin Sino-foreign press corps, four returned from Shenyang in the first group, and twelve returned in the second group. One person is missing. The eight members of the Beiping press corps reached Goubangzi and, upon hearing that the Japanese military was about to occupy Xinmin County, four Chinese reporters turned back and passed through Tianjin on the morning of the 22nd on their way back to Beiping. The four foreign reporters are still proceeding at risk and are reportedly staying at Dahushan. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

Domestic News Telegrams Three

Rong Zhen and Others Escaped

(Beiping) Rong Zhen, Bao Wenxue, and others escaped; they were not released by Japanese soldiers. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

(Beiping) Rong Zhen will publish an article detailing the truth of the incident. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

(Beiping) The families of various key figures in the Northeast Frontier Defense Headquarters escaped on the 19th and arrived in Beiping this morning, some escorted by platoon leader Xiao Mingqing of the Garrison Battalion. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

(Beiping) Rong Zhen, Chen Xingya, and others arrived in Beiping at 1:30 AM this morning and immediately went to the hospital to visit Zhang Xueliang. Zhang Zuolin's sixth wife, carrying her sixth daughter, and the fourth, fifth, sixth, seventh, and eighth sons, along with over ten male and female attendants, all escaped from Shenyang in disguise. Zhang's wife and others were wearing coarse blue cloth clothing and looked haggard. According to those who traveled with Rong, our side did not resist at all after the Shenyang incident. After the Japanese military occupied various institutions in Shenyang, they came to Rong Zhen's residence to search it. Rong escaped through the back door. All the belongings in Rong's residence were loaded and taken away, and eight people were arrested. The former chairman of the province, Zhai Wenxuan, was detained. Yu Zhen and Wu Tailai's son were also detained. The goods in Zhu Guangmu's residence and the residences of Zhai, Wu, and Yu were all looted. Han Yunpeng was shot and killed, and the director of the mortar factory, Li, was killed. All the belongings in the Marshal's Mansion were loaded and taken away. Rong Zhen escaped in disguise as a servant. The arsenal currently has 80,000 rifles, 4,000 machine guns, and the aircraft factory has 200 new and old aircraft. The total losses are estimated at around 100 million yuan. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

British and American Ships at Qinhuangdao

Prevent Japanese Navy Landing

(Beiping) Military news: After two Japanese warships sailed to Qinhuangdao yesterday, one British and one American warship each followed closely behind. The Japanese warships wanted to land, but were unsuccessful due to interference from the British and American warships, and subsequently dropped anchor. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

(Beiping) Reports yesterday that a large number of Japanese troops were coming from Tanggu were inaccurate. However, one Japanese warship has arrived. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

Japanese Kwantung Army

Appoints Zhang Zongchang to Military Post

(Beiping) The Japanese Commander Honjō established the Kwantung Army Headquarters in the Liaoning Provincial Government in Shenyang and appointed Zhang Zongchang as commander of the Kwantung Army Detachment. Zhang himself has already arrived in Lushun and will go to Shenyang within the next few days. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

Japanese Sixth Division

Protects Work on the Tumen-to-Jilin Road

(Harbin) Three thousand Japanese troops have continued to arrive in Longjing Village. Troops from the Sixth Division Headquarters are advancing towards Dunhua to protect work on the Tumen-to-Jilin Road and build a light railway. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

Japanese Military Authorities

Intend to Further Increase Troops in the Eastern Provinces

Japanese Diet to Ratify Troop Dispatch

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs received a telegram from Nagasaki stating that the Japanese military authorities intend to issue a formal mobilization order for Manchuria. However, the cabinet meeting yesterday failed to pass it due to opposition from the Foreign Minister. In reality, the Japanese troops stationed in various parts of Korea have been actively sending troops to Jilin and Liaoning Provinces in recent days, and they are poised to occupy the entire three Northeastern provinces. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

(Tokyo) At today's cabinet meeting, Prime Minister Wakatsuki reported to the Emperor on the government's attitude towards the Manchurian incident. Next, the Minister of the Army reported on the war situation in Manchuria and requested understanding for the dispatch of Korean troops. The cabinet decided to formally approve it. (Telegram from Den Tsū on the 22nd)

(Nanjing) Although the cabinet has already ratified the reinforcements from Korea that went to Manchuria yesterday without government orders, it has now decided not to send any more reinforcements and has ordered the recall of the fifty soldiers who opened up to Jian Island from Korea yesterday. It has also ordered the Japanese military not to proceed north of Changchun. (Reuters Telegram on the 22nd)

(Nanjing) It is reported that when the cabinet met to discuss the continued dispatch of reinforcements to Manchuria, Foreign Minister Kijūrō Shidehara and Minister of the Army Jirō Minami had a fierce debate. Shidehara said that sending more troops to Manchuria would make Japan's actions more like a war. Minami replied that there were many Chinese troops in Manchuria, and he feared that they would far outnumber the Japanese troops. Therefore, reinforcements must be sent to increase the Kwantung Army's fighting power. Minami later added that in order to avoid misunderstandings by foreigners, the current commander of the Kwantung Army, Honjō, had been ordered to cooperate with the local Chinese in administering the municipalities in the various towns occupied, rather than implementing military rule. (Reuters Telegram on the 22nd)

(Tianjin) The 19th and 20th Regiments stationed in Korea are preparing to depart. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

The Japanese Side Intends

To Destroy Northeastern Construction

(Beiping) According to a certain source, the Japanese military is destroying all buildings along the way wherever it goes, causing the Chinese side to suffer significant losses and making it impossible to recover, in order to increase the Japanese influence in the Northeast. (Central News Agency Telegram on the 21st)

Zhang Xueliang

Has Determined Policy Towards Japan

(Beiping) It is reported that Zhang Xueliang has determined a policy to cope with Japan. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

(Beiping) Zhang Xueming returns to Tianjin today. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

(Beiping) Yan Huiqing arrives in Beiping today. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

Huludao Still Peaceful

(Tianjin) The Huludao wireless station reported at 12:00 AM on the 21st that it had detected two warships. The Northeast Fleet used signal lights to inquire about which ships they were, but received no response. They then retreated by 1:00 AM on the 22nd. The island is still peaceful. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

Chen Xingya Talks About

The Japanese Military Entering Shenyang

Wang Yizhe Refuses to Lend Barracks

Street Names in the Shenyang Commercial District Changed

(Beiping) Chen Xingya arrived in Beiping at noon on the 22nd after passing through Shanhaiguan. According to him: (1) Before the incident, a Japanese military officer visited the commander of the First Brigade, Wang Yizhe, and said he wished to borrow the barracks at Beidaying. Wang refused. As soon as the Japanese military officer left, the sound of gunfire and artillery was heard. Wang's troops, in order to avoid conflict, withdrew from the north gate. (2) After the Japanese military entered Shenyang, they changed the names of the streets in the commercial district to "something-something" machi (Japanese for town). (3) On the morning of the 21st, Japanese aircraft strafed the schools in Xinmin County. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

Japanese Military Enters Fushun City

(Harbin) On the evening of the 20th, the 33rd Regiment of the Japanese 20th Division attacked our military barracks in Fushun, killing over 70 of our officers and soldiers and capturing over 100. The Japanese military entered the city on the morning of the 21st. (Telegram from Dian on the 22nd)

Deputy Commander-in-Chief's Headquarters

Announces Shenyang Intelligence

(Beiping) The Commander-in-Chief's Headquarters announced Shenyang intelligence: (1) Under the Mantetsu Laodaokou Bridge, the Japanese military has been installing barbed wire and other obstacles for days. (2) The Shenyang branch of Citibank was looted by the Japanese military and Korean ronin, and two Americans were killed. The American Consul has lodged a serious protest with the Japanese military. (3) A British engineer from the Beining Railway Factory in Huanggu Village, Buckton, was driving to the commercial district on business when he was stopped by the Japanese military under the Laodaokou Railway Bridge and shot at, injuring the chauffeur. The Briton walked back to the factory. (4) Chinese are allowed to enter and exit the Liaoning Japanese station, but no one goes there. (5) Chinese refugees are fleeing with their elderly and young children, their cries shaking the earth, and the situation is extremely tragic. They are fleeing to Huanggu Station to wait for trains to the west. (6) Shops near the Liaoning Central Station have all been looted by the Japanese military and ronin. (7) Chinese are not allowed to watch when entering or leaving various institutions. (8) Eleven Chinese police officers who were killed were transported outside the city by the Japanese military and buried in the industrial district. (9) The Japanese garrison posted a public notice reassuring the people, but the refugees are extremely crowded. The situation is especially chaotic today. The Japanese are in contact with our county government to form a plainclothes team to maintain public order. (10) The shops in the city's commercial district are still closed, and the people are finding it extremely difficult to obtain necessities, and the sources are cut off. (11) The Shenyang-Lushun section of the Shenhai Railway has been dismantled by the Japanese military, and only ten cars can pass between the Yingpan and Chaoyangzhen stations. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

(Beiping) The Deputy Commander-in-Chief's Headquarters received a telegram from the Communications Brigade stating: (1) Japan is continuing to increase troops in the Northeast, expand its war preparations, and deploy military defenses, with the intention of occupying Shenyang for a long time. (2) The Japanese military appointed Tanimura as the mayor of Shenyang. (3) The Japanese military does not recognize Chinese officials, and does not pay attention to any matters involving Chinese people. (4) The Japanese military commissioned the Shenyang County Magistrate Li to form a self-defense force of 800 men, all unarmed. (5) The residences of various dignitaries in Shenyang have been guarded by the Japanese military. (6) The Japanese military will close the Chamber of Commerce and force the stores to open. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

Peacetime Embassy Guards

Engage in Defensive Work

(Beiping) The Beiping authorities have now made preparations. The guards of the Japanese embassy have been busy for the past day or two engaging in sandbagging and other defensive work. (Reuters Telegram on the 22nd)

Jiang Zuobin

Telegraphed That He Has Arrived in Tokyo

(Nanjing) Jiang Zuobin telegraphed the Ministry of Foreign Affairs reporting that he and Counselor Jiang Huaben and First Secretary Ding Shaoji arrived in Tokyo on the 22nd and immediately took office. (Special Dispatch on the 22nd)

(Nanjing) Minister Jiang Zuobin arrived at Tokyo this morning and visited Foreign Minister Kijūrō Shidehara at 3:00 PM, only exchanging greetings upon taking office and not mentioning the Manchurian incident. (Telegram from Den Tsū on the 22nd)

(Nanjing) Minister Jiang arrived at Shinbashi Station at 8:00 AM this morning and immediately went to the embassy. Regarding the Manchurian incident, he said, "The cause of this incident is as the Japanese side said, but guaranteeing occupation also violates international law. It is regrettable that Japan has taken such action in a civilized country. Japan should bear responsibility under international law. " (Telegram from Den Tsū on the 22nd)

Qingdao Authorities

Earnestly Protect Foreign Nationals

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs received a telegram from the Qingdao Municipal Government and Zhang Xueliang, stating that Qingdao has a large number of Japanese residents and is a particularly important location. Since the "September 18th Incident" (Shenyang Incident), the municipal government, in conjunction with the party headquarters and naval forces, has been deliberating on measures to maintain order, with the main principles being composure and tolerance. They are working together, supervising the municipal Public Security Bureau to earnestly protect foreign nationals, strictly preventing reactionary incitement, and engaging with the Japanese consulate in open dialogue to jointly prevent misunderstandings between the people of the two countries. The local order is as peaceful as usual, and the Japanese navy has not engaged in any unauthorized landing or overstepping of boundaries. (22nd Special Dispatch)

(Qingdao) Qingdao is quiet. The Public Security Bureau has recalled the security teams stationed outside the city to maintain public order. The municipal government issued a proclamation on the 22nd, urging citizens to peacefully engage in their occupations and not to easily believe rumors, causing unnecessary alarm. (22nd Special Dispatch)

Glimpses of Various Nations' Attitudes

British and Russian Newspapers Both Advocate Just Discourse

Recognizing Japan's Violation of the Kellogg-Briand Pact

(Nanjing) Diplomatic circles received a dispatch from London stating that the London "Manchester Guardian" editorial advocated League of Nations intervention in the Manchurian incident, stating that Japan's invasion of Manchuria was swift, indicating a well-organized and prepared action. Japanese militarists had long been plotting and vigorously promoting such actions, which endanger the interests of all countries in China and violate the spirit of the Kellogg-Briand Pact. The nations that have signed the non-aggression pact should pay attention to it. (22nd Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) According to a certain source, the U.S. government expressed surprise and concern regarding the Japanese military actions and has been preparing to pay close attention to the military actions in Manchuria. (22nd Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) A telegram from Moscow stated that the Soviet official newspaper commented that Japan's invasion of Manchuria disregards the League of Nations, tramples on the Kellogg-Briand Pact, and violates the Washington Treaty. The Soviet Union has determined that Japan's actions have the tacit approval of imperialists and will swiftly pursue the matter to prevent imperialist aggression from succeeding. The Moscow Party newspaper stated that Manchuria was originally a place of contention for the rights and interests of England, America, Russia, and Japan. This time, Japan's solo invasion may trigger a major war. The world has already seen the effects of war treaties and the League of Nations. The U.S. government's silence is equivalent to destroying the Kellogg Pact itself. The U.S. government will advise the Chinese and Japanese governments based on the non-aggression treaty. The general U.S. public opinion believes that the Washington Treaty signed by various countries in 1922 should be used for the nine countries to discuss solutions to Eastern disputes. (22nd Special Dispatch)

(Washington) State Department officials stated today that they are paying more attention to the Manchurian incident than on Saturday and Sunday. Although no decision has been made on whether to notify China and Japan to respect their obligations under the Kellogg-Briand Pact, the general consensus is to apply the Nine-Power Treaty of 1922 to the Manchurian dispute, as that treaty stipulates that signatory countries should consult each other when disturbances occur in the East. (21st National Telegram)

(Berlin) Although German newspapers are occupied with European affairs, they are paying close attention to the Manchurian incident, but they are only publishing the facts without criticism. However, the opinions of the public and political circles can be summarized by the "Kölnische Zeitung" editorial, which states that Germany deeply regrets and is greatly alarmed by this new dispute but will remain strictly neutral. Germany maintains strong relations with both China and Japan and sincerely hopes that the already turbulent international situation will not be shaken by events similar to war. (21st National Telegram)

All Major Party Members

Unanimously Shoulder National Affairs

No One is Allowed to Rest

Unite to Deal with Foreign Aggression

(Nanjing) On the evening of the 22nd, Wu Tiecheng forwarded another telegram from Guangdong, expressing sympathy for the idea of "fighting against external aggression while resolving internal conflicts" and hoping that the government will reorganize so that all Central Committee members have the opportunity to participate in politics. The previous insistence on "personal issues" has been abandoned. Therefore, Hu Hanmin is welcomed here with righteousness and is no longer allowed to rest, but to manage party affairs. The Guangdong side is also not fixated on the rise and fall of certain key figures. It is said here that in the face of great difficulties, all major party members are not allowed to rest but must come out together to shoulder national affairs and seek a way to save the situation. After yesterday's Mausoleum meeting, key figures are tending towards the idea that everyone should not rest but unite to face external aggression. As for how to unite, they are still waiting for Zhang, Li, and Wu in Peiping to relay information. It is also heard that Guangdong hopes for a government and military commission formed in accordance with the party constitution. (22nd Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Chiang Kai-shek telegraphed Li Shizeng, Wu Tiecheng, and Zhang Ji, urging them to return to Nanjing immediately to discuss peaceful unification and unite against Japan. (22nd Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Liu Tianduo, a counselor of the Examination Yuan and a classmate of Sun Ke, sent a telegram on the 22nd stating that the Japanese are immoral, trampling on our Dong Province and brutally killing our compatriots. If this can be tolerated, what cannot be tolerated? I have heard that you are advocating for peace and jointly relieving national difficulties, to comfort the spirit of the late Premier in heaven and to support the people's anti-Japanese sentiment. At this critical moment, your actions are urgent. (22nd Special Dispatch)

Exhibition Hall Teachers

Ordered to Pursue Liu's Troops

Government General Order

National Mourning

Anti-Japanese Movements Arise Everywhere

(Nanjing) The National Government, upon receiving a letter from the Central Executive Committee, stated that the Japanese soldiers forcibly occupied our territory and killed our soldiers and civilians, a great shame and humiliation, and extreme grief. Yesterday, the committee decided to issue a nationwide circular, ordering all flags to be flown at half-mast for one day on the 23rd of this month and to suspend entertainment banquets to show mourning. On the 21st, an order was issued to all directly subordinate agencies to comply. (22nd Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Party headquarters in Hubei, Yunnan, Hebei, Shanxi, and other provinces and cities, all officers and soldiers of the Second Cavalry Division, the Tianjin Women's Association, and the General Branch in the Philippines, the General Branch in Mexico, and the directly subordinate branch in Liverpool, etc., telegraphed the Central Government one after another, requesting immediate mobilization and a decisive battle with Japan, stating, "Rather than waiting to die, why not fight for survival?" (Nanjing) The Municipal Women's Relief Association decided to organize a Nanjing Women's Anti-Japanese National Salvation Volunteer Team to jointly face the national crisis, and telegraphed female compatriots to organize anti-Japanese national salvation volunteer teams and organize propaganda teams to work in groups. Our army retreats without resistance. In the face of this great change, we must cease internal strife and resist external aggression, working together with one heart and fighting to the end." (22nd Special Dispatch)

New Dutch Envoy Arrives in Beijing

(Nanjing) The newly appointed Dutch Minister to China, de Beukelaer, arrived in Beijing this morning from Shanghai. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs sent the Chief of the Protocol Section, Bi Mingyu, to welcome him at the station. Lindbergh and Wife

Continue Inspecting Disaster Areas

(Nanjing) Mr. and Mrs. Lindbergh continued to inspect the disaster areas west of the Grand Canal today and are scheduled to fly to the provinces afflicted by the Yangtze River disaster on the 23rd to inspect and take many photos of the disaster areas, which will be sent to the Relief Committee for reference. (22nd Special Dispatch)

American Wheat Begins Shipping to China

(Nanjing) Resident Agent in America, Rong Kui, telegraphed that the first batch of American wheat, totaling 30,000 tons, has begun shipping and is expected to arrive in Shanghai before October 10th. After the first batch arrives, the second batch, totaling 60,000 tons, will be shipped immediately. (22nd Special Dispatch)

National Games Likely to be Suspended

(Nanjing) Wang Zhengting, a member of the National Games Preparatory Committee, telegraphed the Preparatory Office today, stating that this year's National Games will be suspended, and the preliminary elections in various provinces will also be suspended to concentrate all efforts against Japan. He also stated that he will suggest this to the Central Government, and it is expected that the Central Government will approve it. After receiving the telegram, the office issued a proclamation announcing the suspension of the preliminary elections in Beijing. (22nd Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Personnel in charge of the National Games said that the recent situation in the Northeast is dangerous and, judging from the current situation, the Games seem unlikely to be held, but no decision has yet been made by the meeting. (22nd Special Dispatch)

Memorial Service for Deceased President Tan

(Nanjing) On the anniversary of the death of deceased President Tan, Lv Bichou, Director of the Secretariat of the Executive Yuan, Xu Jingzhi, Director of Political Affairs, and others led all the staff of the Yuan to the Linggu Temple Cemetery in the early morning to pay tribute. Former colleagues and relatives of deceased President Tan also went to pay tribute, expressing their sorrow. (22nd Central News Agency Telegram)

(Nanjing) The government ordered the Flood Relief Committee to advance one million in cash to cooperate with the Jiangsu Provincial Government to carry out work relief and complete emergency projects for damming and rescue in the shortest possible time. (22nd Special Dispatch)

Liang Guanying's Troops Donate Salaries to Help Relief

(Nanjing) All officers and soldiers of Liang Guanying's troops donated tens of thousands of dollars of salaries to be distributed for emergency relief in Jiangbei and prepared to build embankments with soldiers. (22nd Special Dispatch)

Major Fire on Huashi Street in Beijing Yesterday

(Nanjing) At 3:00 AM on the 22nd, a fire broke out at the Futai Paper Shop on Huashi Street due to electrical wiring, spreading to 28 houses and causing significant losses. (22nd Special Dispatch)

Plan to Improve Agriculture in Disaster Areas

(Nanjing) In order to restore and improve agriculture in the disaster areas, Xu Shiying advocated establishing agricultural cooperatives in the disaster areas and drafted an outline of eight measures to be submitted to the National Government Flood Relief Committee for public decision and implementation, which has been amended and passed. (22nd Special Dispatch)

Jiangsu Provincial Government Meeting

(Zhenjiang) The Jiangsu Provincial Government's regular meeting on the 22nd resolved: (1) Wang Long, the magistrate of Gaoyou County, neglected embankment work and was derelict in his duties and removed from office for investigation. His vacancy will be filled by Li Maozeng, a magistrate who passed the examination. (2) Ni Weiqing, the magistrate of Suining County, left his post without authorization and was removed from office. His vacancy will be filled by Gong Xiwei, the former magistrate of the county. (3) Rui Jiarui, the Director of Education of Rugao County, applied to resign and was approved. His vacancy will be filled by Chen Da, the Director of Education of Jiangdu County. The vacancy left by Chen Da as the Director of Education of Jiangdu County will be filled by Jia Qihuan. (4) The vacancy of the Director of Education of Guanyun County will be filled by Ding Lehui, the current Director of Education of Ganyu County. The vacancy left by Ding Lehui as the Director of Education of Ganyu County will be filled by Wang Zhongbo. (22nd Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The Peiping Peace Relief Association received the press today. National salvation also includes disaster relief. Peace is now hopeful, and the work of this association should be even more intense. Foreign Important Telegrams British Parliament Passes

Suspension of the Gold Standard Act

Various Parties Set Aside Private Views to Jointly Relieve National Difficulties

America and France Express Willingness to Help England Maintain Credit

Securities Transactions in Various Countries Still Mostly Suspended

Reuters, London, 1st day of the month. Chancellor of the Exchequer Snowden proposed in the House of Commons the application of a section of the Suspension of the Gold Standard Act, explaining the reasons for the Cabinet's decision. The opposition proposed rejection, but the House of Commons ultimately passed it by a vote of 275 to 112. Opposition leader Henderson, after Snowden's speech, stated that the Labor Party is willing to do its best to avoid any actions that could cause panic at home and abroad. In fact, British financial strength is, as the Chancellor of the Exchequer said, with no reason for any panic. After the bill was passed on its third reading, it was sent to the House of Lords, where it was proposed by Foreign Secretary Reading and passed completely in two minutes. Shortly thereafter, it was submitted to the British monarch for approval. Since the Labor Party did not oppose the bill, and the Liberal Party held a meeting today originally intended to draft a free trade declaration, it instead issued a statement declaring its willingness to support the National Government's efforts to maintain British credit. These two events show that various parties want to set aside party differences and jointly relieve national difficulties. When Chancellor of the Exchequer Snowden proposed the motion, he said that the plan would not hinder the freedom of the city of London, nor would it hinder the movement of cash deposited in the Bank of England by other governments or banks. The British government still has an obligation to repay cash (referring to US dollar loans) in accordance with the loan terms. The governments of the United States and France have expressed their intention to support British credit, and the British government is very grateful for this. Some foreign debtors of British debts are currently unable to pay due to their own domestic financial situation, and there are reports that the debts owed by the Bank of England to France and the United States are about to expire, and the recent debts of France and the United States will be used up. Therefore, the government has no choice but to make this decision. The British people have not engaged in the export of funds. The government intends to work with foreign banks in London to find ways to prevent the sale of cash, and intends to consider a plan to levy on foreign bonds owned by the people to form a reserve that can be used to maintain the British currency when necessary. They have tested foreign opinions and learned that they do not currently welcome an international conference to seek cooperation from the central banks of various countries, but the British government strongly supports this move and will continue to state the necessity of this move. The internal position of the United Kingdom is currently stable and should maintain its position. Our move may have a serious impact abroad, but it is only temporary. Anyone who trusts the British currency will never regret misusing their trust. The United Kingdom believes that other creditor countries should recognize their responsibility for creating this situation. It hopes that the current turmoil may pave the way for international cooperation. Although the impact of the current situation on countries that rely on London is at least as serious as that on the United Kingdom, international credit institutions may be temporarily disrupted, but the British currency will still be a medium of international credit. If British finances are handled carefully, it does not see any reason for the British currency to fall in the long term. The British government is implementing this plan not to adopt a soaring policy, but to prevent the British currency from falling.

Reuters, Bombay, 21st of the month. All provincial governments in India have announced that they will close tomorrow for one day to prevent financial reactions after the British government suspended the Gold Standard Act. The Calcutta Stock Exchange will be closed until September 24.

Reuters, Amsterdam, 21st of the month. The stock exchange here is closed today due to the British suspension of the Gold Standard Act and will open tomorrow.

Reuters, Paris, 21st of the month. The foreign securities exchange is still not open today. The board of directors decided to strictly enforce the regulations regarding the guarantee of strength on the missing side and ordered the missing side to hand over securities at each sale.

Reuters, London, 21st of the month. British Prime Minister MacDonald said in the House of Commons today in response to a question from a member that the suggestion of using silver as currency to restore trade in the Far East seems unlikely to be implemented.

Reuters, London, 21st of the month. The British Stock Exchange is closed today and will not open tomorrow. The date of resumption will be decided temporarily.

Reuters, New York, 22nd of the month. The New York Stock Exchange Board of Directors met today and decided to prohibit short selling. After the market opened today, important securities all fell by one to five pounds. Foreign securities were all weak, with Belgian 7% bonds falling by ten pounds and German 5.5% bonds falling by three pounds.

Reuters, London, 22nd of the month. Newspapers this morning mostly discussed the question of whether the Labor Party will join the cabinet. Several newspapers said that the possibility of a government change has occurred in the past 48 hours, and the motive is to seek greater national unity. Several other sources said that MacDonald has negotiated with Henderson on the Labor Party joining the National Government. Approximately, if the government agrees to correct the reduction of unemployment benefits, the Labor Party can be expected to cooperate. If so, the current government will be maintained for two years until the end of the parliament.

Their cruelty and tyranny are enraging both humans and gods. They are now advancing towards Yantai and Longkou, provoking everywhere, clearly intending to take advantage of our natural and man-made disasters to plot against our entire country. The life and death of our compatriots hang by a thread. It is hoped that all will rise up in armed resistance, jointly face the national crisis, quickly cease internal strife, and unite to resist Japan, so that China will not immediately sink, and the final calamity can be averted together. This urgent telegram is sent with tears and utmost anticipation. Signed, Zhejiang Provincial No. 1 Middle School, 588 teachers and students.

Internal disasters have not ended, and external troubles suddenly arise.
