Local News 2

Yesterday's News of Disaster Relief in Various Provinces

A Visit to the Disaster Relief Shelter

The Shanghai First Disaster Relief Shelter on Liuying Road, Zhabei, has been completed and is accepting people. Yesterday morning, the Bureau of Social Affairs invited representatives from all walks of life to visit, with over thirty representatives from party and government agencies, various groups, chambers of commerce, newspapers, news agencies, Chinese and Western representatives arriving. Director Pan Gongzhan personally received the visitors. The shelter occupies over thirty-nine mu of land and is divided into two main parts, front and back. The front part is for office, security, fire protection, clinics, wards, storage, supplies warehouse, and material collection rooms. The back part is the residence of the disaster victims. There are rows of sheds on the left and right, each with twenty, totaling forty. Each shed is divided into ten rooms, totaling four hundred, each room can accommodate more than ten people, totaling more than four thousand people. There are also washing and bathing rooms and toilets on both the left and right sides. Two congee meals are served daily in the morning and evening, and lunch is served. Vegetarian food is the most. Each person is given a set of single cloth shirts and pants, a set of cotton clothes and pants, and is given a cotton blanket and straw mat. One Western doctor, two nurses, and one pharmacist are hired to specialize in treatment and medication. The National Medical Association also sends two national doctors every morning and four in the afternoon to diagnose and treat them on site. In addition, the pharmaceutical industry donates medicinal materials and prescribes and decocts prescriptions. A sick ward is set up for the seriously ill to live in and receive treatment. Disaster victims can choose either Western or Chinese medicine at will. Now, as disaster victims arrive in Shanghai in an endless stream, the first shelter is not enough to accommodate them, so a second shelter is being built to its east, and a third shelter is being built on the vacant land of the Commercial Press on Song Park Road, Zhongxing Road. If all three shelters are completed, it will cost about 50,000 to 60,000 yuan to build and can accommodate more than 10,000 disaster victims. The disaster victims in the first shelter come from all over the country, with Jiangsu and Hubei being the most numerous, followed by Jiangxi, Henan, and Anhui, and Shandong and Hunan being the least. As of yesterday, the shelter had a total of two thousand eight hundred and fifty-eight men, women, and children.

Wang Xiaolai's Speech on Disaster Relief

Yesterday, Wang Xiaolai delivered a speech on disaster relief at the XBCL radio station. The speech is as follows: Everyone, today I, Xiaolai, am here to share a few points about the flood disaster with you all. As the old saying goes, "Human affairs affect below, celestial changes respond above." These words are not superstitious, nor do they mean that people have offended the heavens, and the heavens have sent down many disasters. Rather, it means that if people have adequate preparations beforehand for things like floods and droughts, then major floods and droughts will not become a reality. And even if they do become a reality, there will not be tens of thousands of victims drowning and starving to death. Therefore, we have an ancient saying in our country, called "Human determination conquers heaven." This saying is our current motto for overcoming any difficulties. It refers to the current flood disaster. The area affected by the disaster covers seventeen provinces, accounting for one-third of the country's land. There are more than 70 million victims, accounting for one-sixth of the country's population. This has become an extremely serious situation. However, compatriots across the country should remember several historical events in our country. During the time of Emperor Yao, there was a seven-year flood. During the time of Cheng Tang, there was a nine-year drought. But the people at that time did not suffer any major pain. Why is that? Because they were able to prevent disasters beforehand and had adequate remedies afterward. Everyone, imagine that at that time, science was not developed, and transportation was not as convenient as it is now, yet they could still achieve this. Therefore, we now have no fear of not having a solution for such a large flood disaster, but we are afraid that our compatriots across the country who have not been affected by the disaster cannot make a great determination and have sustained efforts. Now, looking at newspapers everywhere, everyone is doing their best for this fundraising effort. There is government relief, group advocacy, newspaper publicity, business profit sharing, and individual frugality. We, who are organizing the fundraising, cannot help but express our deepest gratitude. However, this year's disaster is so large, and there are so many victims, that it is unlikely that the victims can survive by getting through just the next three months of autumn and one winter. Perhaps this relief effort will need to be carried out for a year. Therefore, those who are helping with the relief now need to have a long-term plan, carefully considering their personal income. If a person saves one-tenth or one-twentieth of their monthly income, it is best to temporarily stop saving for the year and use it for monthly disaster relief for the victims. If they have not been saving, then a person's social expenses, cigarettes, and other consumption expenses, more or less, are inevitable. Temporarily stop these social and consumption expenses for the year and use them for monthly disaster relief for the victims. That way, this relief effort will not run out of resources. This is what I have to say to our compatriots across the country who have not been affected by the disaster. Furthermore, we need to plan for the aftermath of the disaster area. The scope of this planning is very large. First, floods and droughts are completely different. After the floodwaters recede, farmers need capital to sow the wheat for the coming year. Merchants want to restore their previous business. Not only have most of the goods they had stored been washed away by the flood, but they also need to purchase new goods. Where will the capital come from? Moreover, there are also debts that are due, and they are being pressed for payment. Organizing disaster relief is already extremely complicated. Talking about the aftermath of the disaster area is even more complex. But if we are afraid of the trouble and do not think of a way to deal with the aftermath of the disaster area, then we do not know how many years this relief effort will need to be carried out before it is completed. Therefore, I, Xiaolai, have a suggestion. When debts are due, we should follow the example of Japan during the Great Earthquake, where commercial organizations in various places, based on local conditions, discussed a proper method of extending the repayment period that would take care of all parties. The capital for stores to resume business will need to rely on the assistance of the banking industry. However, the banking industry in the disaster-stricken areas has suffered such great damage from the flood that it is feared that they will not have much strength. Therefore, for this matter, we cannot but hope that the banking industry outside the disaster area will provide some appropriate assistance to the banking industry within the disaster area. Also, for the capital for farmers to replant winter wheat, I, Xiaolai, believe that we should take two measures. The first is to take a few percent from the relief funds specifically for this purpose. The second is to take 10 million or 5 million from the disaster relief bonds issued by the government and establish farmers' banks in the disaster area to lend to farmers, using the farmers' land as collateral for the loan. This is what I hope all businesses across the country will come together to think of a solution for. There is also the issue of food relief. The surplus grain in the Northeast can subsidize the food supply for the people in our disaster areas. Everyone knows this. A few days ago, the Chamber of Commerce also sent a telegram to the government about this. However, there are still some people who are carefully considering whether the surplus grain in the Northeast can be sold to us on credit in installments, given the financial resources of the Northeast. In fact, this is not a problem. As soon as the floodwaters recede, according to what I, Xiaolai, just said, we can enable them to resume business. At least 20 million people will not need the government to issue rations by name. We are only afraid that this year's fields will have no harvest and there will be no food to buy. Therefore, I dare say that half of the surplus grain in the Northeast is to be used to relieve these people. As for the remaining one or two million people, if they are not given rations by name, they really do not have the ability to buy food themselves. Then, according to what Mr. Lei Yin of the Shishi Xinbao said on the 7th, the official banks of Jilin and Heilongjiang provinces should first pay for the price of wheat and flour, and then the government should repay half in cash and half with disaster relief bonds. It is not an impassable matter. I hope that the disaster relief organizations will all stand up and advocate for this matter. The last thing I want to say is about water conservancy. In fact, what we are talking about now is not really water conservancy, but flood prevention. This time, let's not talk about other places. Just take the lower reaches of the Huai River in Yangzhou as an example. According to the announcement by the local party headquarters and the appeals of the mass organizations, they all say that there were not sufficient preparations for flood prevention materials beforehand. When the incident happened, the flood prevention personnel all ran away. Therefore, this matter really should be attributed to poor human planning. It is exactly in line with the ancient saying, "Human affairs affect below, celestial changes respond above." I, Xiaolai, remember that during the Guangxu period of the Qing Dynasty, the Yellow River breached its banks in Zhengzhou. It took more than 13 million taels of silver to close the breach. At that time, the country's total income was only 70 million taels per year. The funds used for the flood disaster accounted for almost one-fifth of the total annual income. This shows that they were able to pay attention to the situation of river defense. Furthermore, in the Qing Dynasty, the punishment for those responsible for river defense incidents was very severe. We can see from the Donghua Records and private collections of the time that if the Governor-General of the River Conservancy had a major flood in his area, the heavier punishment would be dismissal from office and exile, and the lighter punishment would be to wear a cangue and be displayed to the public on the riverbank. For a senior official to be punished with a cangue and displayed to the public, its effect on punishing derelict personnel was really no less than dismissal from office and exile. Therefore, although the politics of the Qing Dynasty were corrupt, this aspect is indeed worthy of our attention. I, Xiaolai, feel that flood prevention projects are more important than anything else in the future. But there are two prerequisites. First, there must be sufficient funding. Second, there must be strict assessments of river defense personnel at all times, so that these people do not take the lives of our people as a child's play. Everyone needs to stand up and make appropriate suggestions to the government on this matter. I, Xiaolai, have finished what I wanted to say. However, this time, it is not ordinary charitable disaster relief, but disaster relief to save the country and save the nation. Please everyone unite to show the bloody heart of us Chinese people who love our compatriots, love our country, and love our nation.

China International Famine Relief Commission

Report on Inspection of Wuhu Disaster Situation

Mr. Gu Jisheng, Vice President of the China International Famine Relief Commission, previously went to Wuhu with Mr. Lu Bohong as a representative and Mr. Ning Songquan to inspect the flood situation. He returned to Shanghai yesterday. According to Mr. Gu's on-the-spot inspection, the disaster situation in Wuhu is very severe, no less than that in Hankou and Jiangbei. The area has been flooded since July 20, and it has been two months now, and it is increasing every day. Recently, the water level in various places has gradually decreased, but Wuhu has not decreased. Currently, the prosperous areas are submerged by two or three feet at the lower end, and five or six feet at the higher end. In the remote areas, the highest point is about twelve feet. The water color is black and bluish, and there are fears of epidemics. As for the residents in the water, their feet are mostly swollen due to the mixed tides. Mr. Gu and others, accompanied by Magistrate Yu and Zhao, the Director of the Public Security Bureau, traveled by small boat for 120 li. It was a vast expanse of water. The embankment had collapsed completely, and there was no trace to be found. The boat traveled for an hour, and no human trace was seen. Only on the top of a small mountain did they see some refugees. At first, there were not many. The boat carried large steamed buns, which were scattered on the mountain. Unexpectedly, in an instant, the victims hiding in the mountain gully came one after another, gathering hundreds of people. Among them, children without a thread of clothing were everywhere. These victims have been starving for a long time, and cold is out of the question. Fortunately, the weather is still warm now. If it turns cold, they will either die of hunger or of cold. The victims who fled to the roofs of houses and tree tops were calling out for help, but no one responded. They could only sit and wait for death. Mr. Gu, Magistrate Yu, and Director Zhao and others were heartbroken at the sight. Ning Songquan is a businessman who runs a Yongfengyu Cloth Shop in Wuhu, so he often travels between Wuhu and Shanghai. Witnessing the severity of the disaster, he volunteered to donate all his possessions to help the victims. He makes 20,000 large steamed buns every day and distributes them to the victims. He has been doing this for more than 50 days. It can be said that no less than 250,000 victims have prolonged their lives by eating his steamed buns. He is truly enthusiastic. His colleagues in the shop, Xie Shikun, Ruan Dezhong, Cao Youbai, and others, are also very enthusiastic in handling the relief efforts. However, Mr. Ning is not a very wealthy person, and it will be difficult for him to continue. It is truly worrying. There are very few disaster relief agencies in the area. Therefore, Mr. Gu has negotiated with local gentry and merchants, Tao Yutang and Wei Binchen, as well as Western missionary Mr. Pu, to form a branch of the China International Famine Relief Commission to start disaster relief. Wuhu is currently preparing for this. Mr. Gu has returned to the commission to report and it is set to have a meeting today to discuss how to proceed with the plans.

News from the Jiangsu Flood Relief Association

A Letter on Surveying the Disaster in Wujiang: The disaster situation in Wujiang was previously surveyed by Mr. Wu Lingxiao at the request of the association. Here is the reply letter (some omitted above). I investigated the area from outside the North Gate of Wujiang, along the shore of Pangshan Lake, to Hengdang, a distance of more than 50 li. It was a vast expanse of water. All that could be seen were ruined houses and dilapidated walls, with willows drooping all around. Victims were taking refuge on graves and high mounds, crying out in hunger and cold. It was as if one were in a vast sea of waves, no longer knowing that the boat was traveling through 100,000 mu of fertile farmland. The fields along the lake in Damao Port, Wu Lou, and Zhenze were connected to the lake water. Even the higher fields were half-submerged. Mulberry trees were also occasionally submerged in the water. Mei Yan and Pingwang are a little farther from the lake, but the fields are low-lying. The rain god and the wind god successively wreaked havoc, resulting in a strange disaster. Even the higher ground has seen a sharp reduction in harvests. Since the continuous rain for many days, followed by repeated torrential rains, the fields along the lake have been submerged for more than half of the area. On the 25th and 26th days of the eighth month, there were several days of hurricanes, and the lake water suddenly rose by five or six feet. The frightening waves were like thunder and lightning. More than 50 people who were trying to save their property were swept into the water. Houses, huts, livestock, grain, clothing, and other belongings were swept away. The embankments, which were several feet wide and seven or eight feet high, collapsed almost entirely. The victims were sleeping in the open, without clothes or food. There were about seven or eight thousand people. There were many cases of people living in houses that were in the water and could not be moved. This year, the rain occurred every ten days or so. For the sake of the autumn harvest, farmers and business owners borrowed money to pump water, buy bamboo and wood, and nail piles on the embankments to prevent collapse. However, they were eventually destroyed by the hurricane, and there was no harvest. The tens of thousands of gold spent on rescue efforts were washed away by the wind and waves. This is something that has never happened in previous famines. It is estimated that more than 300,000 mu of farmland in Wujiang have been protected from the water and can hopefully yield a 50% harvest. About 170,000 to 180,000 mu have been protected but yielded no harvest. And more than 100,000 mu along the lake have had their embankments collapse and their dikes breached, becoming one with Tai Lake. Those who cultivated this land have become starving people. They cannot survive without immediate relief. Winter is coming soon, and the north wind is biting. We cannot but urgently seek food and clothing from your association. It is estimated that more than 25,000 people will be waiting for relief to survive the winter. More than 100,000 mu of farmland have been mostly destroyed. If repairs are not made, farmers will lose their jobs. In the future, we will have to seek assistance from your association to organize public works relief (some omitted below).

The Water Level in Luhe Rose Again After Receding. The association recently received a letter from Hong Kangxie, the magistrate of Luhe County, which reads: I am writing to inform you that our county has suffered a major flood this year, which has been reported in telegrams. Luhe is located in Jiangbei, connected to the Chu River in the north and the Yangtze River in the south. All the accumulated water has no place to drain other than the Yangtze River. However, the Yangtze River is full of tides, making drainage difficult. According to statistics, the water level has only dropped by three feet in more than two months. Unexpectedly, during the recent tide period, autumn rain continued to fall non-stop for a day and a night. The sky and the ground were wet, and the water level rose by more than eight inches again. It seems that after receding, it will rise again, with no end in sight. In the blink of an eye, the wheat planting season is approaching. If the water is difficult to recede and there is no ability to sow seeds, it is not only worrying that this year's harvest will be bad, but also that there will be another major loss if the wheat planting season is missed. Thinking of this, I am extremely anxious. I am writing this letter to inform you and hope that you will investigate and provide relief as soon as possible to benefit the victims. With utmost anticipation, I address this to the Jiangsu Flood Relief Association.

Employee of Hu Qingyutang

Qian Huaiting Drowned Himself in the Sea

Deep Resentment Between Husband and Wife

The Corpse Was Retrieved by the Life Saving Bureau

Yesterday morning, at about 10:00 AM, a male corpse was found floating in the Huangpu River, south of the Guanchuan at Map Taiwan No. 39, Wusong. He had a monk's head, a long face, and was wearing a dark blue spring-lined short jacket with a white cloth shirt underneath, bone buttons, and gray serge-lined trousers with white calico shorts underneath. He had a leather belt around his waist, white cotton socks, and gray serge leather-soled shoes. After the body was found, it was retrieved by a patrol boat from the Wusong Life Saving Bureau at about 10:00 AM and brought back to the bureau's dock. Only a copper coin was found on the body, and there were no other belongings. Photos were taken and arrangements were being made to provide a coffin and burial services. At that time, Zhou Yunfu, an employee of Hu Qingyutang Pharmacy on Beijing Road in Shanghai, arrived in Wusong and reported to the Life Saving Bureau that his colleague Qian Huaiting had committed suicide by drowning and asked them to pay attention. The bureau sent someone to accompany him to the dock to identify the body. It was confirmed that it was Qian's corpse. Qian Huaiting, the deceased, was 26 years old, from Zhuji. He was an employee of Hu Qingyutang. His family lived at No. 41, Beixing Lane, North Nicheng Bridge. His wife, Wang, was 25 years old and had two sons, the elder three years old and the younger just over a month old. Qian was usually very prudent and taciturn, but his income was very low, and life was quite difficult. Therefore, he often had disagreements with his wife Wang, which made Qian unhappy. Recently, the couple had a dispute over family matters, and Qian developed a pessimistic view of life. At about 1:00 PM on the 19th of this month, he left home with a silk long gown. On the same day, Qian's colleague Zhou Yunfu and others from Hu Qingyutang received a letter from Qian, which said that he owed some debts and asked his brothers to repay them on his behalf after the year-end bonus. The colleagues were very alarmed after reading the letter and immediately searched everywhere, but there was no trace of him. At about 6:00 PM, they went to Qian's home to inquire. At that time, Qian's wife Wang also received a letter from Qian, which said that since they had been married, the relationship between them had not been good, like water and fire. Living together was meaningless. Rather than living together, it was better to sacrifice himself to avoid delaying Wang's youth. He had committed suicide by drowning on the Ningxing Steamer today. Wang and Qian's colleagues were extremely shocked and immediately sent someone to the Sanbei Company Wharf, hoping to persuade Qian to come back. Unfortunately, the Ningxing Steamer had already departed, so there was no way to save him. However, Qian's wife and colleagues still hoped that he would not commit suicide, as there was no confirmation. They continued to search everywhere. Until yesterday morning (the 22nd), the Ningxing Steamer sailed from Ningbo and arrived in Shanghai. Qian's colleagues immediately went to inquire about the ship. It was learned that Qian had boarded the ship on the 19th when it sailed to Ningbo and asked the tea boy to take a jacket to the nearby pawnshop to get money to buy a ticket. When the ship sailed to the mouth of Wusong, Qian went to the deck and jumped into the sea to drown himself. After learning of this bad news, Zhou Yunfu went to Wusong to report to the Life Saving Bureau. After Zhou confirmed that it was Qian's corpse, he hurried back to Shanghai to report to Qian's wife. Because Qian left no property behind, Hu Qingyutang paid for the clothing and coffin. Yesterday afternoon, Qian's colleagues accompanied Wang to Wusong to collect the body. When the coffin was being prepared, Qian's wife cried loudly while holding the coffin, and many of his colleagues shed tears. It was a tragic scene. The coffin is temporarily placed at the Wusong Siming Public Hall and will be transported back to his hometown for burial at a later date.

Wife of Yin Wenlong

Lawsuit Against Airline

Besides Claiming Funeral Expenses

Losses Exceeding Seven Hundred Dollars

Dispute Over Responsibility Issue

Court Adjourns to Announce Verdict on the 29th

Yin Wenlong, a compradore for the Hankou Arnhold, Karberg & Co., specially returned to Shanghai last winter because his wife, Sun Yuefang, was giving birth in Shanghai. Subsequently, on December 9th, he boarded China National Aviation Corporation's Shanghai No. 2 aircraft to Hankou. Unexpectedly, shortly after takeoff, the plane crashed, causing serious injuries and death to all passengers and the pilot. Yin was among the deceased. Later, his wife, Sun, negotiated with the airline, demanding compensation for losses. Because the company firmly refused, she filed a lawsuit with the First Special District Court. After repeated summonses and hearings, the court instructed both parties to reach a settlement, as previously reported. However, the airline consistently maintained that the accident was beyond human control and that it should not be held responsible for the passengers' losses. Therefore, a settlement proved difficult. Yesterday morning, Judge Li Mo held a continued hearing. First, the defendant's lawyer presented documents, stating that these were letters of certification proving that the pilot, Bell, had flying experience, as well as Bell's resume. Subsequently, a Mr. Yao, a ticket seller from the airline's sales department, testified about Yin Wenlong's ticket purchase. He stated that Yin had purchased a ticket on December 3rd for the 4th from Shanghai to Nanjing. Because he still had a round-trip ticket from Nanjing to Hankou, he reminded Yin to pay attention to the passenger regulations printed on the back of the ticket and instructed him to sign the purchased ticket. At that time, Yin stated that he feared he might not be able to travel the next day and that it would be inconvenient to sign the ticket in advance, so he decided to sign it when he departed. Yin also said that he had flown before and was very familiar with the regulations on the back of the ticket. Although he did not sign the ticket, he verbally acknowledged them. On the 4th, Yin did not go and informed the company that he would postpone his trip until the 9th, when he boarded the Shanghai aircraft. According to regulations, the ticket inspector must verify the ticket before the passenger boards the plane. However, on that day, due to time constraints, the ticket inspector did not have time to ask Yin to sign the ticket, so he would have to sign it upon arrival at his destination. This was why Yin's ticket was not signed. Next, the plaintiff's lawyer presented a letter from the manager of Arnhold, Karberg & Co. in Hankou, proving Yin Wenlong's monthly salary and annual commissions during his lifetime. Then, arguments began. First, the plaintiff's lawyer, Liu Shifang, spoke, stating that if the defendant argued that Article 654 of the Civil Code could not be invoked in this case, then it should present a special law. Since there was no special law, the Civil Code should naturally apply. The court should not refuse to hear the case simply because there was no explicit provision. The defendant also argued that the airline was a state-established entity, but its nature was different from other state-owned transportation agencies. The contract signed with the United States stated that it was a limited liability company operating in accordance with the laws of the Republic of China, and its jurisdiction was controlled by the board of directors. If it were state-owned, it would naturally be managed by the Ministry of Communications. Since the deceased did not sign the ticket, he was not bound by the regulations on the back of the ticket. The claims being pursued include funeral expenses, which are documented, and losses exceeding 70,000 yuan, which were estimated by the insurance company based on the deceased's lifetime income and the plaintiff's future life expectancy. If the court considers the calculation to be inaccurate, then it should be re-evaluated. Next, the defendant's lawyer, Li Zuyu, replied, first stating that the accident was caused by force majeure. Second, he said that the Civil Code's provisions for passenger carriers did not include aviation. It was inappropriate for the plaintiff to impose the responsibility of a passenger carrier on the company. Moreover, Yin Wenlong had verbally acknowledged the regulations on the ticket when he purchased it, so the company was not liable for the accident. Finally, he stated that the key point of the case was to resolve the issue of responsibility first. If the company was not held responsible, then the losses claimed by the plaintiff would not be valid. Therefore, the defendant requested a preliminary judgment first. Judge Li then announced the end of the arguments and adjourned the hearing until the morning of September 29th for the verdict.

Autumn Calibration of Measures in the Rice Industry

The Shanghai Rice Industry Rengu Guild and various businesses held an autumn calibration of measures at the Cuixiu Hall of the City God Temple on the previous two days. The guild notified businesses in the north and south to bring their measures for calibration and invited leaders from various rice industry guilds, associations, and groups to supervise. Ye Huijun, chairman of the Bean and Rice Industry Guild, Zhu Zixiang, chairman of the Rice Shop Guild, Yan Xiaoquan, chairman of the Southern Rice Merchant Guild, and leaders of the Changxi Public Office, as well as rice merchants, attended. Twenty measurers were selected to calibrate the measures. When each measure was calibrated, the leaders present verified it. If it was accurate, the Rengu Guild and the Southern and Northern Public Guilds would affix a calibration certificate to the measure and brand it with the words "Autumn 20th Year". To ensure that boatmen knew the secret mark of the brand, rice merchants notified them. It is reported that more than 600 measures were calibrated in the two days, which is more than 100 fewer than in previous seasons. This is because wharves have been built in both the northern and southern markets, allowing rice boats to dock at the wharves and gather in one place, making it easier for businesses to measure rice. Therefore, the number of measures used by businesses has decreased.

Romanian Crimes

Theft and Morphine Trafficking

At around 10 AM the day before yesterday, two Romanians, Boarnsky and Kovsmenko, went to a bookstore on Haig Road in western Shanghai to buy books worth several dollars. They took out a ten-dollar bill to get change. The shop assistant gave them a five-dollar bill. The Romanians claimed that the bill was not usable in the market and asked to exchange it, wanting to choose the bill themselves. The shop assistant took out a stack of bills for the Romanians to choose from, and they took one bill and left with the books. The shop assistant then discovered that seventeen and a half dollars were missing from the bills. Knowing that the Romanians had stolen them, he followed them and saw them enter a house at 3 Avenue Joffre in the French Concession. He immediately reported this to the Jing'an Temple police station. The head of the police station immediately dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives to arrest the two men at the address, along with detectives from the French Concession police station. However, Bo and Kov had already left. The detectives waited at the house, and at around 4 PM, a Romanian named A. Drigin, 25, entered the house looking for Boarnsky. The Chinese and foreign detectives, seeing that he looked suspicious, arrested him. After questioning, they learned that he lived at No. 1 Jing'an Villa. They took him to his home to search it and found a suitcase containing eleven tins of morphine. He was taken to the police station along with his wife, A. Mursina, also Romanian, 24 years old, and they were detained separately. Yesterday morning, Tregan and his wife were sent to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. According to the police station lawyer Wang Yaotang, Boarnsky and Kovsmenko were arrested by detectives from the French Concession police station on Broadway last night because they were also involved in a case in the French Concession. Therefore, they are currently detained at the French Concession police station. He requested that the court send a letter to the Second Special Court to transfer Bo and the others to this case. The confiscated morphine had also been subjected to an unofficial chemical test. The test results showed that only the top layer of each tin was morphine, while the bottom was mixed with valueless white powder and falsely labeled with German company brands. It was necessary to send it to the Shanghai Municipal Council Health Department for an official chemical test and requested a postponement. The morphine was presented to the court. When questioned, the defendants claimed that the morphine had been deposited with them by two Germans, Beto, and that they knew nothing else. They stated that they went to the French Concession to visit Boarnsky to collect seven dollars in gambling debts. After Judge Feng Shide verified their statements, he ordered that the two defendants be remanded in custody and that a letter be sent to the Second Special District Court at a later date to transfer Boarnsky and Kovsmenko for further questioning.

Reader Correspondence

Mr. Shen Gengyao's Question (On Methods of Saving the Country and Dealing with Japan)

Now that national disaster has arrived, how should we save China? This is a very serious and urgent question. The following points are explained for guidance: (1) What attitude should our people take towards Japan in their current position? (2) (Omitted) (3) In China's current crisis of survival, why do people still hold a numb and indifferent attitude? (4) Now that there are many people who want to serve the country because of emotional excitement, how can one be considered serving the country and serving society? Can I be considered serving society as a shop apprentice?

(Reply) The people of our country who have a little knowledge and a little bloodiness will naturally be angry at the unprecedented atrocities that Japan has inflicted on our Northeast. However, fighting Japan desperately is only a temporary emotion and impulse, and it is useless. This full of grief, determination, excitement, and passion must be melted, united, and expanded with calm and calm thought, precise and lasting organization and planning, and proceeded in an effective direction. How can it be effective? Everyone must be prepared to sacrifice, but we must sacrifice in valuable and effective actions. Speaking from the position of our people, what can be done:

First, you must get your own body in good shape before you can talk about sacrifice. Everyone must train individually, and they must also receive public training. Regardless of agriculture, industry, commerce, or academic institutions, they must find ways to provide opportunities for group training. When there are no opportunities for group training, first gather comrades and practice regularly.

Second, make a big determination not to use Japanese goods. We don't need to talk about boycotting Japanese goods eight times. One time without success, please see that Britain's national power is considered powerful. India's Gandhi can soften them. How much ability does Gandhi have? The most powerful thing is to promote the non-use of British goods, especially the fact that he wears Indian homespun cloth in the Indian Governor's Yamen and the British Prime Minister's Yamen. Now, in Japan, just the value of cotton cloth accounts for 70% of the total foreign imports, almost 200 million yuan. The products of Japanese yarn factories in China also amount to almost 200 million yuan. If we all agree not to buy it, this one item will be enough to strangle them. What's more, at the same time, all kinds of things are not used. The reason why the boycott was ineffective in the past is that there was no power from the masses. Despite singing high praises for the boycott, no one was willing to be Gandhi. If everyone is determined to be Gandhi now, are we still afraid of being ineffective?

Third, pay great attention to studying the Northeast problem and the Japanese problem. Maps, books, newspapers, and magazines, anything about the Northeast, should be collected as much as possible and studied carefully. The 92-year-old Mr. Ma Xiangbo said, "To save China, first save the Northeast; to save the Northeast, first know the Northeast."

As for your current job, it is not only directly serving society, but also indirectly serving the country. Because to strengthen the country, you must first enrich the country. Striving to increase production and develop the social economy is simply the fundamental plan to save the country. In the current period of resisting Japan and saving the country, we should work even harder. Look at Germany after the Great War. The workers automatically increased their working hours by one hour every day, so they restored national power so quickly. The fourth point is not a problem.

But the second question should not be said like this. If someone says that, you should strictly correct him. It is not necessarily true that you say that the people of the country are numb and indifferent. Look at how much the people's spirit has been promoted in various places these days, so the third point is also not a problem.

Shen Bao Reader Correspondence Guidelines

The staff of this newspaper firmly believe that you readers each have several personal problems that need to be resolved urgently. Based on the spirit of serving society, the staff are willing to take the position of consultants and, with the utmost sincerity, try to conduct written discussions. If readers can thereby obtain appropriate solutions, reduce some difficulties, and increase some happiness, wouldn't that be a great pleasure?

1. All problems that you want to discuss with the staff of this newspaper are temporarily limited to three items: education, career, and marriage.

2. When corresponding, please first clearly state your surname, given name, gender, age, occupation, or place of study (grade), native place, and mailing address (it is still advisable to open it in detail when continuing to correspond, fearing that the previous letter may not arrive). After that, start a new line and indicate the problem you want to discuss. The text should be detailed, accurate, and easy for people to understand the true meaning. On the outside of the envelope, please write Shen Bao Reader Correspondence Department for collection, and attach a sufficient number of return letters. When corresponding, you must cut out and paste the special issue stamp of the Shen Bao reader correspondence column in the upper left corner of the stationery as proof.

3. How this newspaper handles incoming letters:

A. Respect readers' wishes. All letters stating a desire not to reply in the newspaper or not to disclose names when replying will be followed. B. If the letter does not state how to reply, but the staff believes that replying to one person has the value of providing reference to everyone, it should be disclosed in the newspaper.

C. If the letter states a desire to reply in the newspaper, but is limited by space, it can only be selectively disclosed or even not disclosed, or because the issue is still under consideration, it must be disclosed later. Please forgive us for that. However, if we cannot reply in the newspaper, we will still reply by correspondence.

Lawsuit over Dancer Being Splattered with Feces

Ge Chongxi Did Not Attend Due to Illness

Dancer Demands 1,000 Yuan in Compensation

Sun Aiying, a dancer currently working at the Da Hu dance hall in Jing'an Temple, recently hired lawyer Yuan Yang'an to file a lawsuit in the First Special District Court against Ge Chongxi, the manager of the Paris dance hall, for assault and insult. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Xiao Xiexun presided over the hearing in the Fifth Criminal Court. The defendant, Ge Chongxi, claimed to be ill and did not attend. Lawyer Jiang Baolian attended court as his agent and requested a postponement to prepare for the defense. The plaintiff, Sun Aiying, along with witnesses Wang Xiuying and Chen Huiying and her agent lawyer Yuan Yang'an, appeared in court. Sun Aiying stated the reasons for the lawsuit, saying: "I used to work as a dancer at the Paris dance hall. After my contract expired, I left Paris and accepted a job at the Da Hu dance hall. Two other dancers from Paris, Tu Xiuying and Chen Huiying, also accepted jobs at Da Hu at the same time. The defendant, as the manager of Paris, hated me for leaving and vowed to make things difficult for me. Then, on the evening of the 12th, I hired a car from my residence on Dagu Road to Da Hu. When I passed the intersection of Jing'an Temple Road and Ma Huo Road, four thugs suddenly stopped the car and threw the filthy feces contained in cigarette boxes at my head. They also snatched a embroidered scarf and a jade brooch. The patrolmen investigated, arrested three people, and one person escaped. After taking them to the police station, it was learned that the three people, Zhou Fulin, Shao Genfa, and Ye Zixiang, were invited by the fugitive Zhou Degong. Zhou was instigated by Ge Chongxi, the manager of Paris, and each received five yuan. Qiu Genfa used to be a tea server in Paris, so they knew each other. Now I am accusing Ge of instigating insult and injury, please punish him according to the law, and please compensate for the stolen items and mental damage, totaling 1,000 yuan." Witnesses Wang Xiuying and Chen Huiying testified that they used to be dancers in Paris and left at the same time as Sun to join the Da Hu dance hall. When they left, Ge Chongxi, the manager of Paris, expressed dissatisfaction and said that Sun Aiying should be harmed. However, they did not witness the incident that day. Detective Yang Yunfeng stated the situation of the investigation at that time, but did not provide evidence that Ge instigated the crime when he was interrogated in the police station. The plaintiff's agent, lawyer Yuan, immediately stood up and stated that this point was clarified in the minutes of the last court hearing and requested an investigation. Judge Xiao adjourned the case to be heard again on the afternoon of the 26th of this month.

Free Talk

齋夫 on Conversations Without Eradicating the Garden Grass

The Nobel Prize Drenched in Blood

What is the Nobel Prize? No one in academic circles is unaware of it. Its value is forty thousand US dollars per prize. Five prizes are awarded annually, totaling two hundred thousand US dollars. These five prizes are awarded to individuals who have made the most significant contributions in physics, chemistry, physiology or medicine, literature, and world peace during the year. The prize money comes from the interest generated by eight million four hundred thousand US dollars, which was earned by Nobel throughout his life from manufacturing powerful explosives and smokeless gunpowder.

Alfred Bernhard Nobel, a Swede, was born in 1833 and died in 1896. From the age of seventeen, he assisted his father in manufacturing nitroglycerin. Nitroglycerin barrels were filled with sand. Seven years later, some nitroglycerin accidentally leaked into the sand, giving him a crucial idea. After repeated experiments, he finally created dynamite using 75% nitroglycerin and 25% kieselguhr. This happened in 1867. Later, he replaced kieselguhr with cork, making it even safer. A few years later, he used collodion to treat wounds. Collodion is produced by dissolving guncotton in ether. He accidentally poured leftover collodion from a bottle into nitroglycerin, resulting in the surprising creation of blasting gelatin in 1876. This is what the world calls double-strength dynamite. He invented many types of explosives, including military smokeless gunpowder, and obtained 129 patents. His eight million four hundred thousand US dollars came from this.

Initially, his motivation for manufacturing explosives was solely for quarrying purposes. Later, tempted by the government, Nobel did not hesitate to compromise his dignity as a scientist and create deadly weapons for the military. The establishment of the Peace Prize was an expression of Nobel's repentance in his later years. Laying down the butcher knife and becoming a Buddha on the spot, we should certainly express considerable respect for his change of heart. However, the people killed in the past are not the people saved today, and who dares to say that the people saved today will not be killed in the future? The power to determine the life and death of humanity is truly in the hands of scientists. Using science to nurture people instead of killing people is the duty of scientists. If one studies science with the intention of killing, then one is the greatest evildoer in the world. Nobel's repentance is evident to all. His annual blood-soaked prize serves as a warning bell for young scientists. How can we turn a deaf ear to it? If one's eyes are only focused on the forty thousand gold dollars, is that not utterly foolish?

A Word of Wisdom

— Qiu Shui

If a person had a healthy body and a secret to guaranteed success, he would surely become a dullard incapable of joy, anger, sorrow, and happiness.

A person's intelligence is not measured by the abundance of their experience but by the degree of their ability to acquire experience.

The acquisition of experience is purely based on knowledge. Experience is the mother of success, and knowledge is the father of success. Both are indispensable.

What the world calls greatness is what religion calls holiness. Both are things that can be hoped for but not attained.

First love between a man and a woman is a combination of curiosity and foolishness.

What is life? It is nothing more than constantly cutting open one's soul to exchange it for worthless things.

Put the time of mourning and the effort of silent prayer into work, and China will have a day of revitalization.

If humans did not have the psychology of worshiping idols, there would no longer be specialized technical talents in the world.

Excerpts from Lectures

— Zhou Cailiang

Recently, there has been much talk about scientific management in our country. This is because neither production nor consumption can be discussed in economic terms without it. Recently, the Shanghai Chinese Vocational Education Society, recognizing the needs of society, established a Department of Industrial and Business Management. The other day, they specially invited Mr. Cao Yunxiang, the former president of Tsinghua University, to the school to lecture on "Personnel Management Issues." His profound insights and apt metaphors were fully expressed. His words are worthy of reference for society, so I have recorded them below.

Since the National Government promulgated and implemented the Factory Law, most capitalists have been greatly alarmed because they feel their own knowledge is insufficient and are eager to recruit talent to help them. What you are learning today can be said to be exactly what is needed. It goes without saying that after graduation, your career prospects will be bright. However, what I want to tell you today are the various practical problems that urgently need to be solved. For example, a certain bank where my friend Mr. Dai works suddenly had a female employee who repeatedly requested sick leave five or six months ago and did not return for a long time. After repeated investigations by a certain gentleman from the personnel management department of the bank, the truth gradually became clear. The family of the woman in question was very simple, with only an elderly mother in her sixties living with her. An older sister had already married. The woman felt that she still had no home to go to and was saddened by the thought of who her mother would rely on. She became extremely depressed, which led to her illness. When she was ill, there were many consolations, and she felt happy spiritually. The investigator, knowing the details, reported to the bank manager, who ordered the mother to accompany her on trips to various places to relieve her boredom. As a result, she recovered from her illness and returned to work, as diligent as ever. From this, it can be seen that the way to care for people cannot be overlooked.

My Views on Disaster Relief Work

— Tianxu Wosheng

The Shanghai newspapers of September 19th reported that the Shanghai Disaster Relief Office announced to the city's industrial and commercial sectors: "This office has taken in over three thousand male and female disaster victims from northern Jiangsu, Hubei, Anhui, and Jiangxi. They are fed every day but have nothing to do, which is not appropriate. Setting up factories would be too expensive, and we do not have the resources at the moment. Therefore, we are publishing this notice, appealing to the industrial and commercial sectors to show compassion for the disaster victims who have lost their jobs and homes. If you have any work that requires labor, please share it with the disaster victims to help them." I believe that if this strategy can be implemented, it would indeed be the best way to solve the problem. However, whether it can be implemented depends first on allaying employers' concerns. Then, not only can the industrial and commercial sectors accommodate them, but even households needing to hire workers would not need to hire through brokers. Large households in Shanghai often employ more people than they have family members. They provide food and lodging and pay generous wages, enough for a comfortable living with surplus. If residents of the city need any workers, they should specify the origin, gender, and approximate age required, as well as the type of work skills needed and the monthly wage, and send a letter of inquiry to the Disaster Relief Office. It is expected that among the three thousand people, many will assess their capabilities and volunteer. The office would then select them, register them in order, categorize them according to their work skills, inquire about the addresses of relatives, and record them in the remarks column. They would then issue a letter of introduction, provide clean clothing and bedding, and send them to try out the work. The office would also specify the guarantee conditions on the letter of introduction for the employer. If there are any cases of theft, absconding, or illegal behavior, the office would be fully responsible. In this way, the employer would have no concerns, as the guarantee would be more reliable than that of a broker. Once they pass the trial period, they would have food, clothing, and shelter, and they could even save a portion of their wages and get insurance to secure their future. In this city of three million people in Shanghai, taking in three thousand disaster victims would be like only one person supporting one other person.

In Memory of the Author of "The Sound of Silence"

— Xu Xinqin

The French scholar Mr. Louis Laloy has studied Oriental languages for many years. He enjoys delving into ancient Chinese books, especially the theories of ancient philosophers like Lao Tzu, Zhuangzi, and Huainanzi. He is particularly interested in and well-versed in ancient Chinese music and opera. He has translated Chinese operas and authored the book "Chinese Music," which is well-known in the West. In 1914, he published the article "Huainanzi and Music" in the Dutch journal "T'oung Pao," which revealed insights that had not been previously expressed by either Chinese or Western scholars. This astonished Chinese and Western scholars of Sinology. Recently, Mr. Laloy was commissioned by the French government to come to China to investigate culture and ancient music. Before his departure, he wrote the article "The Sound of Silence" (Preface to a Visit to the Ancient Music of Divine China), published in the Parisian newspaper "Le Temps," expressing his admiration for ancient Chinese culture. Yesterday, through the introduction of the returning artist Mr. Liu Haisu and the literary critic Mr. Fu Lei, I was able to meet Mr. Laloy at Mr. Li Shizeng's villa. At that time, Mr. Chu Minyi, Mr. Li's nephew, and others invited prominent figures such as Mr. Cai Zimin, Mr. Gao Lu, and academic giants from the Chinese and French communities in Shanghai, totaling over forty people, to attend a tea party. The musicians Mr. Zheng Jinwen and professors from the Datong Music Society and the National Conservatory of Music were invited to perform ancient music suites to welcome Mr. Laloy. After listening, I was able to read Mr. Laloy's great work, "The Sound of Silence." The setting sun cast scattered shadows. Mr. Zheng then played the ancient melodies of the Two Han Passes. The night was quiet and the sounds of nature were silent. The sublime music was moving. Thoughts arose in my mind. I took up my pen to write this epilogue, expressing my feelings. I will now record Mr. Laloy's great work below.

The Sound of Silence (Preface to a Visit to the Ancient Music of Divine China)

— Written by Louis Laloy of France

This is the time of the sound of silence. To those who understand music, it is the most beautiful sound. We are shaken by the noises of the city and burdened by material things, and eagerly seek a way to refresh our minds. In the second century BC, after the end of the war between Rome and Carthage but before the conquest of Gaul, Liu An, the Prince of Huainan and a member of the Han imperial family, once said: "To see the invisible is to find what is seen. To hear the soundless is to find what is heard. The ultimate taste is not satisfying. The ultimate word is not ornate. The ultimate joy is unknown. The ultimate sound is not called... To hear the sound of sound is sound. To hear the sound of silence is wisdom. Without sound, without wisdom, one communicates with the divine." Although the arguments are different, the spirit is the same. "The zither does not sound, yet the twenty-five strings respond with their respective tones. The axle is not connected, yet the thirty spokes each rotate with their strength. The strings have fast and slow, large and small, and then a melody is formed. The chariot has labor and leisure, movement and stillness, and then it can reach far. What makes the sound is the soundless. What can reach thousands of miles is the motionless." The zither is now the highest instrument in China. In the seventeenth century, there were zither techniques that included not only the light plucking and slow kneading of the fingers but also the key to nourishing the mind. The dexterity of the wrist is not enough to achieve a clear and lofty artistic conception. "If the mind is chaotic, the hand is clumsy. If the hand is clumsy, the zither is not still. Only the quiet and determined spirit of a reclusive hermit can achieve stillness. The heart is far from the mundane, and the hand is naturally at ease. Those who burn incense retain its fragrance and drive away its odor. Those who brew tea take its mellow taste and remove its richness. If you want to seek pure sound, you should also cleanse your heart and eliminate worldly desires. The fingers should sweep away all worldly air, and the strings will naturally be clear and ethereal." This long journey is intended to visit this ancient music that still exists today. I will read the books of the sages, meditate deeply, cultivate my mind and nurture my spirit, hoping that the people of that country will not abandon me. The way to control water is to exert effort on the ditches, so that they can follow their nature and each find its place. This is the way to absorb it, and it should be broadened. As for the industrial and commercial sectors, there is a great need for people, and among the three thousand people, all kinds of skills will be available, and each will have a specialty. When I served in the military and political sectors, I often saw military officers and prison officials who, when they needed people for work, could immediately select talents from the military and prisons. For large projects such as construction engineering, everything from earthwork and hardware to painters was often available. For small tasks such as tailors, cooks, laundresses, and gardeners, they could all be summoned immediately. There were even scribes, scholars, painters, artisans, doctors, diviners, and astrologers among them. So, are these three thousand people necessarily lacking in skills other than sleeping and eating? Therefore, I sincerely hope that a government-run job placement center will be established and announced quickly, with extensive advertising, not limited to disaster victims. Everyone should be allowed to register, so that talent will be gathered and supply and demand will be matched. The panic of unemployment will also be relieved, which is beneficial to society and people's livelihood. This is what I truly hope for. (Moved to help disaster relief.)

The Rotary Club's Perspective

A Husband's Wife (21)

— Jiang Hongjiao

Madam Li had long had such thoughts in her mind, but she had never spoken of them to anyone, nor had she heard anyone else say them. Madam Li felt that Mr. Chen's argument was a profound truth. She was moved as if struck by electricity and greatly admired Mr. Chen. However, since she had met Mr. Chen, she had never praised him or complimented him. She even wanted to refute him with irrelevant words to test whether his opinion of her was truly genuine, because she suspected that he might be acting, trying to stir her heart and make her sincerely want to be his good friend.

"That cannot be generalized. The opposite of obligation is right. How can you forget that? Are there no mutual rights between husband and wife? Sometimes one party is willing to sacrifice their rights and only fulfill their obligations. Then what is there to argue about? You cannot just take us as an example. Our example is not necessarily universal," Madam Li said, feeling better and deliberately arguing with him.

"Friends' obligations are probably limited and have a time limit, but the rights and obligations of husband and wife are absolutely unlimited and timeless, so it is very easy to become tired and resentful. But in my opinion, rights and obligations are a kind of commercial transaction, only emotion is a kind of spiritual bond, so there is no such thing as obligation and right. This is the case with husband and wife, and it is also the case with friends. For example, you just straightened my clothes for me. I did not ask you to do it, but you did it voluntarily. You have no obligation to straighten this clothes for me, but I have enjoyed the right. When you did it, you did not expect me to repay you in any way, but I have already thanked you. I don't necessarily have to say thank you to you, but you are not unhappy because of this. This is because the relationship between friends is an intimate relationship. If my wife were in front of me, and I asked her to straighten my clothes for me, and she did it, I would feel that this was her obligation and my right. If she did not do it, I would feel that she was not fulfilling her obligation, or she would dislike me for blaming her, and I should not enjoy so many rights, and then there would be unpleasant feelings, and perhaps a dispute would arise. So I say it is still friends, who can understand each other relatively easily. Because I think more thoroughly, I don't restrain my wife too much, nor do I forbid her from associating with male friends. I think the more husband and wife, the less interesting. If you have fulfilled your obligations and are willing to sacrifice your rights, it already contains a component of resentment. It is great to sacrifice yourself without knowing that you have sacrificed yourself," Mr. Chen explained to Madam Li like a scholar lecturing on the philosophy of life. He had never told his wife this kind of view, because he felt that his wife's level was not up to such talk. Only Madam Li, he thought, could be discussed in detail, so he spoke frankly.

Madam Li was of course a smart woman. She admired his eloquence and felt that it was sweeter than ordinary love words. She regretted not having met him before she got married. She hated her own fate, only meeting Mr. Li. She fantasized about how happy she would be if she had a husband like Mr. Chen. Now that he said this, perhaps he also resented not having met me earlier. Thinking of this, she just smiled shallowly and nodded slightly.

"You won the championship in this debate, and I have failed," Madam Li said, sitting up and brushing the beautiful hair on her temples behind her ears, revealing her fair neck, which was truly beautiful.

However, after that, each session gradually improved, because most shorts took the opportunity to cover, causing the market to be supported. By the afternoon, it gradually opened and improved. It was rumored that a large short account close to a certain factory was still rushing to cover, so people's hearts were shocked, and the buying momentum was very strong. However, in terms of the environment, it still feels not optimistic, because the exchange rate has lengthened, and foreign wheat can continue to be determined. It is heard that four ships of Russian wheat were again opened the day before, with a combined price of only three taels and six qian and a half. Although the violent acts of Japan have not been resolved, there is certainly no problem with orders with foreign countries. As a result, September and October fell by one fen and two li and a half compared to the previous day, November fell by one fen and a half, and December to February fell by one fen and two li and a half.

As a result, this month was slightly lower by one fen compared to the previous day, October to December were better by two fen, January was better by three fen, and February was lower by one fen and five gold

Social News

Japan Firmly Adheres to Three Nautical Miles Territorial Waters

Statement of Second Reply

According to the Eastern News, the Chinese side advocates that 12 nautical miles be the territorial sea. In response, the Japanese government sent a second reply to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the content of which insists on three nautical miles and declares absolute opposition to the Chinese side's 12 nautical mile proposal.

Suicides in Germany Increase Again

Due to the Pressure of the Economic Crisis

Berlin News: The black tide of economic instability has surged among the German people in recent years, and ordinary wage laborers are the most affected. As a result, phenomena such as increased suicides, divorces, reduced birth rates, and increased crime have increased greatly. This year, suicide incidents in Berlin have occurred up to seven times a day. After the bank turmoil in July, suicides increased again, mostly due to the loss of savings. According to a survey by the Commercial Research Institute, during the so-called Stinnes crisis in 1924-1925, the national average number of suicides was 50 per day, accounting for 26 to 28 out of every 100,000 people. By the world economic crisis in 1929, 29 out of every 100,000 people committed suicide. During the darkest period of last winter, an average of 68 people committed suicide every day. According to the Berlin Collection Report, there was a period during the war when the number of casualties was not so high.

Over 10,000 Boxes of Russian Goods Sampled and Transported to Southern China

North Manchuria Imports 24 Million Yuan of Russian Goods Harbin News: Since the implementation of the Soviet Russian kerosene five-year plan, kerosene production has greatly increased. By the final year of the five-year plan in 1933, its production can be increased to 150 million boxes. Therefore, the Soviet Union is actively preparing for a large-scale dumping policy. A 1.2 million yuan oil storage pool was recently built in Harbin. In the future, the Soviet Union's kerosene dumping in the Northeast will be surprising. In the first half of this year, the amount of Russian goods imported through Manchuria and Suifenhe reached 24 million yuan. Its aggressive business strategy has been noticed by the general public. Recently, the Soviet Russian state-owned trading company loaded over 10,000 boxes of Russian goods samples onto German ships and transported them to Southern China.

Marshal Foch of France

European War Diary Translated by Gu Angruo

After three hours of bombardment, the French Franchet d'Espèrey Army Group began its offensive between Diksmuide and the Lys River at 5:30 AM on September 28th. They achieved a great victory, completely capturing the first line of German defenses, and the second line was greatly shaken.

The next morning, I went to the Franchet d'Espèrey Army Group, visited General Plumer of the American forces in Cassel, met with King Albert of Belgium in La Panne, and then went to Houthem to see Major General Gillain. I urged them to advance rapidly towards Lillers and Hazebrouck. The morale of the troops was not slack. On the 29th, Diksmuide was recovered, and the Bixschoote Ridge and the important towns of Messines and Wytschaete successively fell. Within two days, 10,000 prisoners were captured, along with 200 artillery pieces.

On the 30th, progress continued, but the advance was slightly slowed by rain. However, the British Second Army had already approached Menin and advanced to the left bank of the Lys River.

On October 1st and 2nd, orders were given to temporarily halt the advance in order to re-establish contact with the rear and then intensify the offensive.

Movement in the war zone was difficult. The terrain was riddled with shell holes, filled with mud and water. Several sections of the supply line on the right bank of the Yser River had already been cut off, and in some places, soldiers on the front lines were unable to receive food and ammunition. It was necessary to temporarily use aircraft to transport supplies. To enable the supply convoys to move, the transportation routes had to be thoroughly repaired. In several places, elevated roads, several miles long, had to be built.

Although movement was difficult, the achievements of our army in the Franchet d'Espèrey Army Group were already significant. Fearing the advance of the Franchet d'Espèrey Army Group north of the Lys River and the simultaneous advance of the British Army south of the Sensée River, the German forces retreated before the British Fifth Army (commanded by General Birdwood). The British Fifth Army was operating on the right flank of the British Second Army and had established contact with the First Army. (To be continued)

Youth Corner

Our Expectations

— Jingzhai

The reason why we, the Jing'e Drama Society, are here to perform "A Patriotic Heart" at the invitation of the Lu City Exhibition can be simply stated in two points. First, of course, we want to contribute our very limited strength to appeal for our afflicted compatriots, so that they can receive some tangible benefits and spiritual comfort – material relief. But more importantly, the second point is that I sincerely want to use the only valuable thing we young people have, our boiling passion, to awaken the inspiration of our numb and insensitive compatriots who are still asleep in the dark.

We still remember that in the first issue of the "New Era" weekly, we published an article titled "Our Experience." In this article, on the one hand, we outlined our experience and the structure of our organization. At the same time, we also clarified our goals and our attitude. We said these words: "Drama can satirize life, regulate life, and symbolize life, represent life, and even guide life." In addition, I also stated more clearly in the article "After Seeing The Liar" in this column on June 20th, "We know that the significance and mission of the drama society movement is not only to achieve maturity in technical aspects, but its greatest and most important significance lies in its ability to stimulate a social effect. Therefore, here, all comrades who are striving for the drama movement must know that our success is multifaceted and must contain a central consciousness. As for the perfect and wonderful expression and the intricate and profound plot, these are still secondary issues." Regarding these two points, the former can be said to be our understanding of the true meaning of drama, and the latter can be said to be the goal of our efforts in the drama movement. This has always been considered reasonable by us from the beginning of our work to the recent present, especially in this year – when natural disasters and man-made calamities, internal troubles and foreign invasions, are intertwined, it should be considered that our understanding and the path we are taking are correct and there is no mistake.

But we are just ordinary young people without strength, only with a passion and sincerity. Therefore, when we hear and see the suffering and groaning of the tens of thousands of afflicted compatriots, and the shocking and heartbreaking sight of our homeland stained with the blood of our compatriots flowing from the guns and bayonets of strong neighbors, how heartbroken and angry we are!

However, perhaps because our nation has suffered too deep and too great stimulation and pain, most people seem to have lost their senses and become numb. Perhaps it is fundamentally because the national self-strengthening consciousness of our great Chinese nation has disappeared. Otherwise, why is it that in the face of this natural disaster and foreign invasion, none of us are willing to be invigorated, abandon all our prejudices, and work together to use a death-defying will to fight for the survival and growth of our nation at this critical moment?

Because of this continuous internal turmoil, we think of the afflicted compatriots in the thirteen provinces who are in rags and crying for help. And because of the dark shadows of the afflicted compatriots in the thirteen provinces who are in rags and crying for help, we also think of the occupation of the thousands of miles of our good land, stained with fresh blood. Furthermore, because of the pain of the occupation of this thousands of miles of our good land, stained with fresh blood, we cannot help but think of a few lines in the play "A Patriotic Heart." Akiko is a Japanese woman who married a Chinese man. For the benefit of her own nation and country, she does not hesitate to force her dearest husband and son to be traitors, cause the subjugation of their country, and become slaves, saying, "I love my Japan." At the same time, our two compatriots, the husband and son, although under this extremely distressed and oppressive force, finally gave us a cry of resistance like a lion's roar.

("I love my China.")

From this, we can gain a new understanding and awakening. We can know that even between those as close as husband and wife, mother and son, inevitable conflicts can arise due to the interests of their own country and nation. Then, are those clichés and stale tunes of "maintaining East Asian peace," "same script, same race," and "Sino-Japanese friendship" that exist only in words and on white paper still worth our blind faith and admiration? Look, the three eastern provinces are the territory of our Republic of China, but now they have been forcibly swallowed and plundered by the violent Japanese. It is time for us to wake up. We should support the soul of our nation, which is on the verge of death, and we should all shout in resistance,

("We love our China.")

Oh, when we think of this place, the dark shadows of the afflicted compatriots who are in rags and crying for help, and the tragic sight of a scorched earth covered in blood and flesh, reappear before our eyes. We are heartbroken, we are angry, and we do not know how we will dedicate ourselves. Oh, we can only offer you fresh blood and a passionate heart, praying that all our compatriots can, from now on, have a determination to "I love my China," and hope that everyone will contribute their strength to help our afflicted compatriots and to resist the enemy of the entire Chinese nation, Japan.

Autumn is Here

— Huo Biao

On Saturday evening, Wei came to my residence. He has obviously become much thinner recently. Although we can still find a trace of innocent smile on his face from time to time, it quickly fades away and often disappears, making it impossible to grasp. Over the past month, we two seemed to have speculated a lot for a certain need, and gradually changed from sparse to dense. The intimacy of this kind of conversation, even we ourselves could not have imagined that our friendship would have such progress. Tonight, he caught a very excited look, but he was panting, his cheeks with some drunken look, and an unnatural emotion reflected the ripples on his heart lake.

"Long, let's take a walk in the park," he said as soon as he stepped in, "It's too stuffy in the room, it doesn't soothe my heart."

"What's wrong?" I had doubts about his hasty attitude. "You seem very excited, but what new attack have you suffered, you are taking it seriously, right?"

"There's nothing to take seriously, my friend, let's talk in the park."

He took my hand, so we walked slowly. The park is less than a hundred steps away from my residence, but it took about a quarter of an hour. On the way, we listened to the sad cries of the autumn cicadas. Suddenly, Wei clenched my hand and said,

"Friend, autumn is here," the tone was desolate, as if with infinite meaning.

"Oh..." I was speechless for a moment, as if my soul had been violently awakened. I couldn't know why my friend would talk about the problem of "autumn is coming," and I didn't even know how a resonance of sorrow would occupy our air. I thought, I groped...

With a "swish," several yellow leaves fell in front of us. We laughed foolishly at each other, everything was contained in silence.

Entering the park gate, Wei said to the scene in front of him after only a few steps,

"Alas, the god of desolation, has the face changed in just a few days? Has the fiery warmth disappeared?"

"That's right," I blurted out unconsciously, "This is the authority of autumn."

We skimmed over some sparse figures, avoided some scattered hustle and bustle, and chose a secluded high pier to sit down.

Wei's expression was changing, it was as if all kinds of thoughts were lurking in his heart, but we were all afraid to speak. Unnecessary loneliness was active around us, and we were ashamed that we couldn't immediately break the gap between us.

I gazed at the boundless sky, I overlooked the shadows of the trees, I held my breath and wanted to speak, but a certain kind of invasion, invisible, made me want to stop again. Tonight, I stirred up Wei's scars that I hadn't warmed for a long time, but in the end I couldn't maintain the silence. Wei said with a repentant tone, "I can't let her leave me, if I lose her, my life will have no light, no hope..."

"That was last autumn," he paused for a while and then continued, "It was also such an evening that I discovered that she had been seduced by another man, so I was indescribably frustrated and suffered a sickness. I killed the heart to possess her, and from then on, I didn't want to see her again. We have been separated forever. But, until I die, I will always love her. Her hair, her dimples, her gentleness, all her contours..." He spoke in the tone of performing a play.

"But since then," he continued, "The interest in my life has decreased. Alas, how will I place my love? Now that autumn is here again, where can I find peace?"

I listened to his words that were inspired by the depression, and I didn't know whether to sympathize with him or to grieve my own life. I secretly wiped away tears, but I couldn't say it as straightforwardly as he did, as if it was vomiting blood.

"So for the coming of this autumn wind," he said again, "I can only think of escaping. This situation really can't make you settle down, and all life is tied to the rotating machine of contradiction."

"Friend, let's be more objective," I tried to calm down, "Women are... Pursuing her will only lead you to the abyss of pain."

"However..." We will abandon women for the rest of our lives..."

"Of course it's not saying that," I defended, "But rather than being in love with a woman who doesn't understand love, I think it's better to refuse."

"..."

"..."

The cool wind blew past, and we were unconsciously silent for a long time, as if intoxicated, and as if deeply disgusted.
