Book and Newspaper Introductions

Introduction to Statistical Methods

— Shuyuan

Author 丨丨丨丨 Xu Binghan

Statistics, as an independent science and as an important subject recognized by the general public, has only been around for the past fifty years. The main purpose of this book is to describe the statistical methods used in modern times and to provide scholars with a basis to follow. The book is divided into four parts and seventeen chapters.

The first chapter describes a brief history of statistics. Before 3500 BC, Egypt had compiled household and wealth registers to build the pyramids. Then in 4400 BC, Rameses II, in order to eliminate the abuses of uneven land distribution and redistribute the land, compiled a land statistical table of Egypt. This is the beginning of statistics. At that time, the purpose of compiling statistical tables was to assist the government in administrative convenience and military strategy, so the calculations were all ordinary materials such as taxes, land distribution, and the number of soldiers. Until the mercantile era (merchantilistic Perild), statistics made great progress. Because the government at that time worshiped monetarism, it had to encourage the country's industry and commerce on the one hand, and had to seek exports exceeding imports on the other hand. The various laws and regulations that arose from this need had to rely on accurate statistics to determine their legislative policy, so statistics became more and more important at that time. Since then, the longer the time, the wider the scope of statistical tables has become. In the recent three or four decades, the compilation of statistical tables has become more precise. Almost all modern powers have established statistical bureaus. The National Bureau of Statistics of the United States is an example.

In this chapter, the modern statistical community is divided into two major categories, one is statistical method and the other is applied statistics. The so-called method statistics not only pays attention to the research of special methods, but also pays attention to the manufacture of general laws (Laus), rules (Rules) and methods (Mothods). Applied statisticians apply the laws and formulas created by methodologists to existing concrete facts. It can also be divided into scientific and descriptive, like the population statistics of the United States, which not only compares the people and resources in a certain time in various parts of the country, but also compares them with the population and resources decades ago. This is the best example of descriptive statistics. Scientific statistics often uses recording past materials to construct certain physical or psychological laws.

In the second chapter, the definition of statistics is described. The definitions given by many experts are collected together and carefully verified. Finally, a broader definition is determined as follows: Statisticians are those who judge the collective phenomena of nature or society based on the results obtained from the analysis of calculations or the collection of estimates.

The third chapter describes the functions, characteristics and materials of statistics. The function of statistics is not only valuable to politicians and entrepreneurs, but also theoretical economists and scientific investigators must use statistics to prove their theories or assumptions. Therefore, biologists use this to prove the laws of change and inheritance, and economists use this to establish rules for population, wages, and prices, or to express the causal relationship between different phenomena of each group, such as the relationship between financial panic and unemployment. Sociologists use this to prove the relationship between crime, poverty, suicide and other related phenomena. These are all functions of statistical science. As for the characteristics of statistics, it lies in its ability to simplify complexity. The various things in a group can give us an accurate concept without the tediousness of counting them one by one. For example, to investigate the average wage of workers in this country, there is no need to count the work of each worker. If we can find a few model examples and get their average, we can know the general idea. There are several methods for collecting statistical materials. One is the personal collection method. The investigator personally investigates, can know the situation of the investigation, and is created by one hand, and can get accurate benefits. This method is mostly applicable to natural sciences, and is also used in the investigation of sociology and economics. There is also a method, that is, the investigator hires many recorders or correspondents, and collects the results of their calculations or estimates, or the statistician collects the results of the calculations or estimates of private statisticians and compares them, examines them, and gets the final result. However, the statistics obtained by applying this method are not very accurate, so most of the numerical research work on economics or sociology must rely on government reports, because only the government has the financial resources and will to collect true statistics on the activities of the people of the whole country. Moreover, government statistics can exercise the power to force people to report, but individuals cannot. This is another point where government statistics are superior to private statistics.

The fourth chapter describes the solutions to practical problems, such as defining the scope of the problem and selecting the problem factors. These are extremely important for statistics.

The fifth chapter is dedicated to describing the statistical unit. Statistics often cannot be separated from numbers, and numbers must first determine the unit, and the final unit must be consistent with the name of the unit. Sometimes the nouns cannot be fully determined, then an exact definition must be given to this unit. Choosing a statistical unit not only requires the definition to be correct, but also its nature must be measurable. Abstract things should be expressed in concrete words to facilitate measurement.

The sixth chapter describes the design and collection of statistical materials. Here we are told that there is a characteristic of statistical work, that is, everything must be considered in advance, the origin of errors must be prevented in advance, and the general results must be estimated in advance. All problems, factors, units, assumptions, tables, recorders, tabulation, working methods, time, expenses, etc., are issues that should be carefully considered in advance. As for the methods of collecting materials, the following four are commonly used: (1) personal investigation, (2) estimation by correspondents, (3) forms are filled out by the respondents, (4) forms are processed by recorders. Which of these four methods should be used is appropriate, depending on the nature of the problem, the accuracy of the desired results, and the amount of funds available.

The seventh and eighth chapters discuss the accuracy of statistics. Possible accuracy can be obtained based on various mathematical calculations.

The ninth chapter is about the first analysis problem after the materials are collected – tabulation. There are very detailed instructions on the title and style of the table.

The tenth chapter is about the function of diagrams. Although the numbers in the table can be neat and orderly, they are not convenient for memory or comparison. The main purpose of statistics is to make numerous numbers clear and understandable, so that people can know at a glance. To achieve this goal, there are methods of supplementing or explaining, and diagrams are the most common method.

The eleventh chapter is about the function and classification of frequency tables. When we study various natural phenomena, we find that each group has its own characteristics. Therefore, there is a method of group research, and the table created is called a frequency table.

Chapters twelve to fourteen describe the shortcomings and advantages of various counting methods. There are many formulas in it, which can be used to obtain accurate results.

An important part of statistics lies in the comparison of phenomena in various periods. There are many methods of comparison. The fifteenth chapter describes historical statistics, divided into (1) absolute number tables, (2) absolute historical statistical diagrams, (3) logarithmic statistical tables, (4) logarithmic historical statistical diagrams, (5) index numbers, (6) historical statistical diagrams of index numbers.

The sixteenth chapter describes various methods of comparison. The ultimate goal of all statistical research is comparison. The so-called comparison is to show the relationship between things in time and space, so that we have a clear concept of it. There are very precise numerical explanations for the drawing methods of various charts in comparison.

The last chapter is about the relationship between each other, which means that there is a certain causal relationship between two continuous series or two groups of things. The relationship between each other can be divided into the same relationship and the opposite relationship. There are many tables in this chapter, all of which are very precise.

In this book, in addition to describing the history of statistics, all the shallow methods related to statistics, which are indispensable for the research or tabulation of simple statistical materials, are discussed in great detail. Other analysis and comparison methods are also included without omission. I dare say that this book is a good reference book for practical statisticians, especially in the social sciences. At the end of the book, there are many charts, all of which are very precise and rare.
